States state symbols">\n          Lists of United States state symbols\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Michigan\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">\n            m\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xca\x83/: \'sh\' in \'shy\'">\n            \xca\x83\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\n            \xc9\xa1\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\n            \xc9\x99n\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <small class="nowrap">\n         (\n         <span class="unicode haudio">\n          <span class="fn">\n           <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Michigan.ogg" title="About this sound">\n             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n            </a>\n           </span>\n           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/En-us-Michigan.ogg" title="En-us-Michigan.ogg">\n            listen\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         )\n        </small>\n       </span>\n       ) is a\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        state\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region" title="Great Lakes region">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">\n        Midwestern\n       </a>\n       regions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state\'s name, Michigan, is of\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       origins (form of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ojibwe_language" title="Ojibwe language">\n        Ojibwe\n       </a>\n       word)\n       <i>\n        mishigamaa\n       </i>\n       , meaning "large water" or "large lake".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiB-pdf_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MiB-pdf-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">\n        tenth most populous\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">\n        50 United States\n       </a>\n       , with the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">\n        11th most extensive\n       </a>\n       total area, and the largest state by total area east of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">\n        Mississippi River\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [b]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s capital is\n       <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       , and its largest city is\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">\n        Detroit\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is the only state to consist of two\n       <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">\n        peninsulas\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Lower Peninsula of Michigan">\n        Lower Peninsula\n       </a>\n       , to which the name Michigan was originally applied, is often noted to be shaped like a\n       <a href="/wiki/Glove#Mittens" title="Glove">\n        mitten\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Upper Peninsula of Michigan">\n        Upper Peninsula\n       </a>\n       (often referred to as "the U.P.") is separated from the Lower Peninsula by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Mackinac" title="Straits of Mackinac">\n        Straits of Mackinac\n       </a>\n       , a five-mile (8\xc2\xa0km) channel that joins\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">\n        Lake Huron\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">\n        Lake Michigan\n       </a>\n       . The two peninsulas are connected by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Bridge" title="Mackinac Bridge">\n        Mackinac Bridge\n       </a>\n       . The state has the longest\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">\n        freshwater\n       </a>\n       coastline of any political subdivision in the world, being bounded by four of the five\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       , plus\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Saint_Clair_(North_America)" title="Lake Saint Clair (North America)">\n        Lake Saint Clair\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA-CRM_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOAA-CRM-10">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As a result, it is one of the leading U.S. states for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recreational_boat" title="Recreational boat">\n        recreational boating\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan also has 64,980 inland lakes and ponds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A person in the state is never more than six miles (9.7\xc2\xa0km) from a natural water source or more than 85 miles (137\xc2\xa0km) from a Great Lakes shoreline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area was first settled by\n       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       tribes and later colonized by French explorers in the 17th century and became part of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">\n        New France\n       </a>\n       . After France\'s defeat in the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">\n        French and Indian War\n       </a>\n       in 1762, the region came under British rule, and was ceded to the newly independent United States after Britain\'s defeat in the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       . The area was part of the larger\n       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">\n        Northwest Territory\n       </a>\n       until 1800, when western Michigan became part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Territory" title="Indiana Territory">\n        Indiana Territory\n       </a>\n       . In 1805, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Territory" title="Michigan Territory">\n        Michigan Territory\n       </a>\n       was formed, and in 1837 was admitted into the Union as the 26th state. It soon became an important center of industry and trade in the Great Lakes region and a popular\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant" title="Immigrant">\n        immigrant\n       </a>\n       destination.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although Michigan has come to develop a diverse economy, it is widely known as the center of the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">\n        automotive industry\n       </a>\n       , being home to the country\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(automobile_manufacturers)" title="Big Three (automobile manufacturers)">\n        three major automobile companies\n       </a>\n       (whose headquarters are all within the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detroit_metropolitan_area" title="Detroit metropolitan area">\n        Detroit metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       ). While sparsely populated, the Upper Peninsula is important for tourism thanks to its abundance of natural resources, while the Lower Peninsula is a center of\n       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">\n        manufacturing\n       </a>\n       , services, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-tech" title="High-tech">\n        high-tech\n       </a>\n       industry.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6">\n         <a href="#Government">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Government\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#State_government">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             State government\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Law">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Law\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Politics">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Politics\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Administrative_divisions">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Administrative divisions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Geography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Geography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Climate">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Climate\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Geology">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Geology\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a href="#Demographics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Demographics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Population">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Population\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Birth_data">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Birth data\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#Languages">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Languages\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Religion">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Religion\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#Taxation">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Taxation\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21">\n           <a href="#Agriculture">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Agriculture\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Tourism">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Tourism\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#Transportation">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Transportation\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 Canadian international crossings\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Railroads">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Railroads\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Roadways">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Roadways\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27">\n           <a href="#Airports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Airports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Large_cities.2C_townships.2C_and_metropolitan_areas">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Large cities, townships, and metropolitan areas\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30">\n         <a href="#Culture">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Culture\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31">\n           <a href="#Arts">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Arts\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-32">\n             <a href="#Music">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               9.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Music\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-33">\n             <a href="#Performance_arts">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               9.1.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Performance arts\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34">\n           <a href="#Sports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">\n         <a href="#State_symbols_and_nicknames">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           State symbols and nicknames\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36">\n         <a href="#Sister_regions">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sister regions\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40">\n         <a href="#Bibliography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Bibliography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           16\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Michigan_history" title="Timeline of Michigan history">\n        Timeline of Michigan history\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Michigan" title="History of Michigan">\n        History of Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When the first European explorers arrived, the most populous tribes were\n       <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">\n        Algonquian peoples\n       </a>\n       , which include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Anishinaabe" title="Anishinaabe">\n        Anishinaabe\n       </a>\n       groups of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ojibwe" title="Ojibwe">\n        Ojibwe\n       </a>\n       (called "Chippewa" in French),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottawa_(tribe)" title="Ottawa (tribe)">\n        Odaawaa/Odawa (Ottawa)\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potawatomi" title="Potawatomi">\n        Boodewaadamii/Bod\xc3\xa9wadmi (Potawatomi)\n       </a>\n       . The three nations co-existed peacefully as part of a loose confederation called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Three_Fires" title="Council of Three Fires">\n        Council of Three Fires\n       </a>\n       . The Ojibwe, whose numbers are estimated to have been between 25,000 and 35,000, were the largest.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Ojibwe were established in Michigan\'s Upper Peninsula and\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan" title="Northern Michigan">\n        northern\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Michigan" title="Central Michigan">\n        central Michigan\n       </a>\n       , and also inhabited\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       , northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">\n        Wisconsin\n       </a>\n       , southern\n       <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">\n        Manitoba\n       </a>\n       , and northern and north-central\n       <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">\n        Minnesota\n       </a>\n       . The Ottawa lived primarily south of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Mackinac" title="Straits of Mackinac">\n        Straits of Mackinac\n       </a>\n       in northern,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Michigan" title="Western Michigan">\n        western\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Michigan" title="Southern Michigan">\n        southern Michigan\n       </a>\n       , but also in southern Ontario, northern Ohio and eastern Wisconsin, while the Potawatomi were in southern and western Michigan, in addition to northern and central Indiana, northern Illinois, southern Wisconsin and southern Ontario. Other Algonquian tribes in Michigan, in the south and east, were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mascouten" title="Mascouten">\n        Mascouten\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Menominee" title="Menominee">\n        Menominee\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami_(tribe)" title="Miami (tribe)">\n        Miami\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sac_people" title="Sac people">\n        Sac\n       </a>\n       (or Sauk), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Meskwaki" title="Meskwaki">\n        Fox\n       </a>\n       , and the non-Algonquian\n       <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">\n        Wyandot\n       </a>\n       , who are better known by their French name, the Huron.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">\n        17th century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pere_Marquette.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1686" data-file-width="2096" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pere_Marquette.JPG/220px-Pere_Marquette.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pere_Marquette.JPG/330px-Pere_Marquette.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pere_Marquette.JPG/440px-Pere_Marquette.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pere_Marquette.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          P\xc3\xa8re Marquette and the Indians\n         </i>\n         (1869),\n         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wilhelm_Lamprecht&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wilhelm Lamprecht (page does not exist)">\n          Wilhelm Lamprecht\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       French\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Voyageurs" title="Voyageurs">\n         voyageurs\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Coureur_des_bois" title="Coureur des bois">\n         coureurs des bois\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       explored and settled in Michigan in the 17th century. The first Europeans to reach what became Michigan were those of\n       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Br%C3%BBl%C3%A9" title="\xc3\x89tienne Br\xc3\xbbl\xc3\xa9">\n        \xc3\x89tienne Br\xc3\xbbl\xc3\xa9\n       </a>\n       \'s expedition in 1622. The first permanent European settlement was founded in 1668 on the site where P\xc3\xa8re\n       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Marquette" title="Jacques Marquette">\n        Jacques Marquette\n       </a>\n       established\n       <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Michigan" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan">\n        Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan\n       </a>\n       as a base for Catholic missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Missionaries in 1671\xe2\x80\x9375 founded outlying stations at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Ignace,_Michigan" title="Saint Ignace, Michigan">\n        Saint Ignace\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marquette,_Michigan" title="Marquette, Michigan">\n        Marquette\n       </a>\n       . Jesuit missionaries were well received by the area\'s Indian populations, with relatively few difficulties or hostilities. In 1679,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Cavelier,_Sieur_de_la_Salle" title="Robert Cavelier, Sieur de la Salle">\n        Robert Cavelier, Sieur de la Salle\n       </a>\n       built\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Miami_(Michigan)" title="Fort Miami (Michigan)">\n        Fort Miami\n       </a>\n       at present-day\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph,_Michigan" title="St. Joseph, Michigan">\n        St. Joseph\n       </a>\n       . In 1691, the French established a trading post and Fort St. Joseph along the St. Joseph River at the present day city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Niles,_Michigan" title="Niles, Michigan">\n        Niles\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">\n        18th century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_1718.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1006" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Michigan_1718.jpg/220px-Michigan_1718.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Michigan_1718.jpg/330px-Michigan_1718.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Michigan_1718.jpg/440px-Michigan_1718.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_1718.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Approximate area of Michigan highlighted in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guillaume_de_L%27Isle" title="Guillaume de L\'Isle">\n          Guillaume de L\'Isle\n         </a>\n         \'s 1718 map\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1701, French explorer and army officer\n       <a href="/wiki/Antoine_de_la_Mothe_Cadillac" title="Antoine de la Mothe Cadillac">\n        Antoine de la Mothe Cadillac\n       </a>\n       founded\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Pontchartrain_du_D%C3%A9troit" title="Fort Pontchartrain du D\xc3\xa9troit">\n        Fort Pontchartrain du D\xc3\xa9troit\n       </a>\n       or "Fort Pontchartrain on-the-Strait" on the strait, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       , between lakes\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Saint_Clair_(North_America)" title="Lake Saint Clair (North America)">\n        Saint Clair\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">\n        Erie\n       </a>\n       . Cadillac had convinced\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">\n        King Louis XIV\'s\n       </a>\n       chief minister,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Ph%C3%A9lypeaux_(1643-1727)" title="Louis Ph\xc3\xa9lypeaux (1643-1727)">\n        Louis Ph\xc3\xa9lypeaux, Comte de Pontchartrain\n       </a>\n       , that a permanent community there would strengthen French control over the upper Great Lakes and discourage\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">\n        British\n       </a>\n       aspirations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The hundred soldiers and workers who accompanied Cadillac built a fort enclosing one\n       <a href="/wiki/Arpent" title="Arpent">\n        arpent\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tbaytel_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tbaytel-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-histdet_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-histdet-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (about 0.85 acres (3,400\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), the equivalent of just under 200 feet (61\xc2\xa0m) per side) and named it\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Pontchartrain" title="Fort Pontchartrain">\n        Fort Pontchartrain\n       </a>\n       . Cadillac\'s wife, Marie Th\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa8se Guyon, soon moved to Detroit, becoming one of the first European women to settle in the Michigan wilderness. The town quickly became a major\n       <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">\n        fur-trading\n       </a>\n       and shipping post. The\n       <i>\n        \xc3\x89glise de Saint-Anne\n       </i>\n       (Church of Saint Ann) was founded the same year. While the original building does not survive, the congregation continues to be active today. Cadillac later departed to serve as the French governor of Louisiana from 1710 to 1716. French attempts to consolidate the fur trade led to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fox_Wars" title="Fox Wars">\n        Fox Wars\n       </a>\n       involving the\n       <a href="/wiki/Meskwaki" title="Meskwaki">\n        Meskwaki\n       </a>\n       (Fox) and their allies versus the French and their Native allies.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the same time, the French strengthened\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Michilimackinac" title="Fort Michilimackinac">\n        Fort Michilimackinac\n       </a>\n       at the Straits of Mackinac to better control their lucrative fur-trading empire. By the mid-18th century, the French also occupied forts at present-day\n       <a href="/wiki/Niles,_Michigan" title="Niles, Michigan">\n        Niles\n       </a>\n       and Sault Ste. Marie, though most of the rest of the region remained unsettled by Europeans. France offered free land to attract families to Detroit, which grew to 800 people in 1765, the largest city between Montreal and New Orleans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="448" data-file-width="506" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif/215px-Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif/323px-Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif/430px-Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif 2x" width="215"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Province_of_Quebec_1774.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763-1791)" title="Province of Quebec (1763-1791)">\n          Province of Quebec\n         </a>\n         in 1774\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       From 1660 until the end of French rule, Michigan was part of the Royal Province of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">\n        New France\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [c]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1760,\n       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">\n        Montreal\n       </a>\n       fell to the British forces ending the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">\n        French and Indian War\n       </a>\n       (1754\xe2\x80\x931763). Under the 1763\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       , Michigan and the rest of New France east of the Mississippi River passed to Great Britain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">\n        Quebec Act\n       </a>\n       was passed in 1774, Michigan became part of the British\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763-1791)" title="Province of Quebec (1763-1791)">\n        Province of Quebec\n       </a>\n       . By 1778, Detroit\'s population was up to 2,144 and it was the third largest city in Quebec.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       , Detroit was an important British supply center. Most of the inhabitants were French-Canadians or Native Americans, many of whom had been allied with the French. Because of imprecise cartography and unclear language defining the boundaries in the 1783\n       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">\n        Treaty of Paris\n       </a>\n       , the British retained control of Detroit and Michigan after the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       . When Quebec split into Lower and Upper Canada in 1791, Michigan was part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Ontario" title="Kent County, Ontario">\n        Kent County\n       </a>\n       , Upper Canada. It held its first democratic elections in August 1792 to send delegates to the new provincial parliament at Newark (now\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niagara-on-the-Lake,_Ontario" title="Niagara-on-the-Lake, Ontario">\n        Niagara-on-the-Lake\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFarmer_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFarmer-22">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under terms negotiated in the 1794\n       <a href="/wiki/Jay_Treaty" title="Jay Treaty">\n        Jay Treaty\n       </a>\n       , Britain withdrew from Detroit and Michilimackinac in 1796. Questions remained over the boundary for many years, and the United States did not have uncontested control of the Upper Peninsula and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drummond_Island" title="Drummond Island">\n        Drummond Island\n       </a>\n       until 1818 and 1847, respectively.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">\n        19th century\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">\n        War of 1812\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Territory" title="Michigan Territory">\n        Michigan Territory\n       </a>\n       (effectively consisting of Detroit and the surrounding area) was surrendered after a nearly bloodless\n       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Detroit" title="Siege of Detroit">\n        siege\n       </a>\n       in 1812. An attempt to retake Detroit resulted in a severe American defeat in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Raisin_Massacre" title="River Raisin Massacre">\n        River Raisin Massacre\n       </a>\n       . This battle is still the bloodiest ever fought in the state and had the highest number of American casualties of any battle in the war. Ultimately, Michigan was recaptured by Americans in 1813 after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Erie" title="Battle of Lake Erie">\n        Battle of Lake Erie\n       </a>\n       . An invasion of Canada which culminated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Thames" title="Battle of the Thames">\n        Battle of the Thames\n       </a>\n       was then launched from Michigan. The more northern areas were held by the British until the peace treaty restored the old boundaries. A number of forts, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Wayne_(Detroit)" title="Fort Wayne (Detroit)">\n        Fort Wayne\n       </a>\n       were built in Michigan during the 19th century out of fears of renewed fighting with Britain.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s,_by_Jenney,_J_A_(detail).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1412" data-file-width="1141" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg/170px-Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg/255px-Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg/340px-Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s%2C_by_Jenney%2C_J_A_%28detail%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hauling_at_Thomas_Foster%27s,_by_Jenney,_J_A_(detail).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lumbering" title="Lumbering">\n          Lumbering\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">\n          pines\n         </a>\n         in the late 1800s\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The population grew slowly until the opening in 1825 of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">\n        Erie Canal\n       </a>\n       connecting the Great Lakes and the Hudson River and New York City. The new route brought a large influx of settlers, who became farmers and merchants and shipped out grain, lumber, and iron ore. By the 1830s, Michigan had 80,000 residents, more than enough to apply and qualify for statehood.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A Constitutional Convention of Assent, led by\n       <a href="/wiki/G._Mott_Williams" title="G. Mott Williams">\n        Gershom Mott Williams\n       </a>\n       , was held to lead the territory to statehood.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Progress_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Progress-23">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In October 1835 the people approved the Constitution of 1835, thereby forming a state government, although\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        Congressional\n       </a>\n       recognition was delayed pending resolution of a boundary dispute with\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Toledo_War" title="Toledo War">\n        Toledo War\n       </a>\n       . Congress awarded the "Toledo Strip" to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       . Michigan received the western part of the Upper Peninsula as a concession and formally entered the Union on January 26, 1837. The Upper Peninsula proved to be a rich source of lumber, iron, and copper. Michigan led the nation in lumber production from the 1850s to the 1880s.\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_railroads_in_Michigan" title="History of railroads in Michigan">\n        Railroads\n       </a>\n       became a major engine of growth from the 1850s onward, with\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Detroit" title="History of Detroit">\n        Detroit the chief hub\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A second wave of French Canadian immigrants settled in Michigan during the late 19th to early 20th century, particularly in lumbering areas in counties on the Lake Huron side of the Lower Peninsula, such as the Saginaw Valley, Alpena, and Cheboygan counties as well as throughout the Upper Peninsula with large concentrations in Escanaba and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Keweenaw_Peninsula" title="Keweenaw Peninsula">\n        Keweenaw Peninsula\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first statewide meeting of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican Party\n       </a>\n       took place July 6, 1854, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson,_Michigan" title="Jackson, Michigan">\n        Jackson, Michigan\n       </a>\n       , where the party adopted its platform. The state was heavily Republican until the 1930s. Michigan made\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Michigan in the American Civil War">\n        a significant contribution\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       and sent more than forty regiments of volunteers to the federal armies.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Modernizers and boosters set up systems for public education, including founding the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       (1817; moved to Ann Arbor in 1837), for a classical academic education; and Michigan State Normal School, (1849) now\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Michigan_University" title="Eastern Michigan University">\n        Eastern Michigan University\n       </a>\n       , for the training of teachers. In 1899, it became the first normal college in the nation to offer a four-year curriculum. Michigan Agricultural College (1855), now\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">\n        Michigan State University\n       </a>\n       in East Lansing, was founded as the pioneer land-grant college, a model for those authorized under the Morrill Act (1862). Many other private colleges were founded as well, and the smaller cities formed high schools late in the century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">\n        20th and 21st centuries\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ford_Motor_Company" title="History of Ford Motor Company">\n        History of Ford Motor Company\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="393" data-file-width="512" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg/220px-B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg/330px-B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg/440px-B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B-24_bomber_at_Willow_Run.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         B-24s under construction at Ford\'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Willow_Run" title="Willow Run">\n          Willow Run\n         </a>\n         line, 1942\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s economy underwent a transformation at the turn of the 20th century. Many individuals, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Ransom_E._Olds" title="Ransom E. Olds">\n        Ransom E. Olds\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Dodge" title="John Francis Dodge">\n        John\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Horace_Elgin_Dodge" title="Horace Elgin Dodge">\n        Horace Dodge\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_Leland" title="Henry Leland">\n        Henry Leland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Dunbar_Buick" title="David Dunbar Buick">\n        David Dunbar Buick\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bourne_Joy" title="Henry Bourne Joy">\n        Henry Joy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Brady_King" title="Charles Brady King">\n        Charles King\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">\n        Henry Ford\n       </a>\n       , provided the concentration of engineering know-how and technological enthusiasm to start the\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_automobile" title="History of the automobile">\n        birth of the automotive industry\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ford\'s development of the moving\n       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">\n        assembly line\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Highland_Park,_Michigan" title="Highland Park, Michigan">\n        Highland Park\n       </a>\n       marked the beginning of a new era in transportation. Like the\n       <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">\n        steamship\n       </a>\n       and railroad, it was a far-reaching development. More than the forms of public transportation, the automobile transformed private life. It became the major industry of Detroit and Michigan, and permanently altered the socio-economic life of the United States and much of the world.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the growth, the auto industry created jobs in Detroit that attracted immigrants from Europe and migrants from across the United States, including those from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        South\n       </a>\n       . By 1920, Detroit was the fourth-largest city in the US. Residential housing was in short supply, and it took years for the market to catch up with the population boom. By the 1930s, so many immigrants had arrived that more than 30 languages were spoken in the public schools, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic" title="Ethnic">\n        ethnic\n       </a>\n       communities celebrated in annual heritage festivals. Over the years immigrants and migrants contributed greatly to Detroit\'s diverse urban culture, including popular music trends, such as the influential\n       <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">\n        Motown Sound\n       </a>\n       of the 1960s led by a variety of individual singers and groups.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg/220px-Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg/330px-Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg/440px-Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Headquarters_of_GM_in_Detroit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Detroit" title="List of tallest buildings in Detroit">\n          Skyscrapers\n         </a>\n         in downtown Detroit\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Michigan" title="Grand Rapids, Michigan">\n        Grand Rapids\n       </a>\n       , the second-largest city in Michigan, is also an important center of manufacturing. Since 1838, the city has also been noted for its furniture industry and is home to five of the world\'s leading office furniture companies. Grand Rapids is home to a number of major companies including\n       <a href="/wiki/Steelcase" title="Steelcase">\n        Steelcase\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Amway" title="Amway">\n        Amway\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Meijer" title="Meijer">\n        Meijer\n       </a>\n       . Grand Rapids is also an important center for\n       <a href="/wiki/GE_Aviation_Systems" title="GE Aviation Systems">\n        GE Aviation Systems\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan held its first\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_primary" title="United States presidential primary">\n        United States presidential primary\n       </a>\n       election in 1910. With its rapid growth in industry, it was an important center of union industry-wide organizing, such as the rise of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">\n        United Auto Workers\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1920\n       <a href="/wiki/WWJ_(AM)" title="WWJ (AM)">\n        WWJ (AM)\n       </a>\n       in Detroit became the first radio station in the United States to regularly broadcast commercial programs. Throughout that decade, some of the country\'s largest and most ornate\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Detroit" title="List of tallest buildings in Detroit">\n        skyscrapers\n       </a>\n       were built in the city. Particularly noteworthy are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fisher_Building" title="Fisher Building">\n        Fisher Building\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Place" title="Cadillac Place">\n        Cadillac Place\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Building" title="Guardian Building">\n        Guardian Building\n       </a>\n       , each of which is a\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">\n        National Historic Landmark\n       </a>\n       (NHL).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1927 a school bombing took place in\n       <a href="/wiki/Clinton_County,_Michigan" title="Clinton County, Michigan">\n        Clinton County\n       </a>\n       ; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bath_School_disaster" title="Bath School disaster">\n        Bath School disaster\n       </a>\n       , which resulted in the deaths of 38 schoolchildren, constitutes the deadliest mass murder in a school in U.S. history.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan manufactured 10.9 percent of total United States military armaments produced during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , ranking second (behind\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       ) among the 48 states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Detroit continued to expand through the 1950s, at one point doubling its population in a decade. After\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , housing was developed in suburban areas outside city cores; newly constructed U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate Highways\n       </a>\n       allowed commuters to navigate the region more easily. Modern advances in the auto industry have led to increased automation, high tech industry, and increased suburban growth since 1960.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is the leading auto-producing state in the US, with the industry primarily located throughout the\n       <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">\n        Midwestern United States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario,_Canada" title="Ontario, Canada">\n        Ontario, Canada\n       </a>\n       , and the Southern United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAM_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAM-28">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With almost ten million residents, Michigan is a large and influential state, ranking tenth in population among the fifty states. Detroit is the centrally located metropolitan area of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megalopolis" title="Great Lakes Megalopolis">\n        Great Lakes Megalopolis\n       </a>\n       and the second-largest metropolitan area in the U.S. linking the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       system.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg/220px-Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg/330px-Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg/440px-Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biomedical_Science_Research_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Biomedical Science Research Building at the UM Medical School supports the\n         <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Life_Sciences_Corridor" title="Michigan Life Sciences Corridor">\n          Michigan Life Sciences Corridor\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Metro_Detroit" title="Metro Detroit">\n        Metro Detroit\n       </a>\n       area in\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Michigan" title="Southeast Michigan">\n        Southeast Michigan\n       </a>\n       is the state\'s largest metropolitan area (roughly 50% of the population resides there) and the eleventh largest in the USA. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids_metropolitan_area" title="Grand Rapids metropolitan area">\n        Grand Rapids metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Michigan" title="Western Michigan">\n        Western Michigan\n       </a>\n       is the state\'s fastest-growing metro area, with over 1.3\xc2\xa0million residents as of 2006.\n       <a href="/wiki/Metro_Detroit" title="Metro Detroit">\n        Metro Detroit\n       </a>\n       receives more than 15 million visitors each year. Michigan has many popular tourist destinations, including areas such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Frankenmuth,_Michigan" title="Frankenmuth, Michigan">\n        Frankenmuth\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Thumb" title="The Thumb">\n        The Thumb\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Traverse_City,_Michigan" title="Traverse City, Michigan">\n        Traverse City\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Traverse_Bay" title="Grand Traverse Bay">\n        Grand Traverse Bay\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan" title="Northern Michigan">\n        Northern Michigan\n       </a>\n       . Tourists spend about $17\xc2\xa0billion annually in Michigan supporting 193,000 jobs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yousef_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Yousef-29">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan typically ranks third or fourth in overall\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_%26_development" title="Research &amp; development">\n        Research &amp; development\n       </a>\n       (R&amp;D) expenditures in the US.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MEDC1_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MEDC1-30">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSF_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSF-31">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state\'s leading research institutions include the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">\n        Michigan State University\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University" title="Wayne State University">\n        Wayne State University\n       </a>\n       which are important partners in the state\'s economy and the state\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/University_Research_Corridor" title="University Research Corridor">\n        University Research Corridor\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_Research_Corridor_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-University_Research_Corridor-32">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s public universities attract more than $1.5 B in research and development grants each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bruns_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bruns-33">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Agriculture also serves a significant role, making the state a leading grower of fruit in the US, including blueberries, cherries, apples, grapes and peaches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MIAG_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MIAG-34">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">\n        Government\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Michigan" title="List of Governors of Michigan">\n        List of Governors of Michigan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_delegations_from_Michigan" title="United States congressional delegations from Michigan">\n        United States congressional delegations from Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:71msc_1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="525" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/71msc_1.jpg/170px-71msc_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/71msc_1.jpg/255px-71msc_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/71msc_1.jpg/340px-71msc_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:71msc_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Capitol" title="Michigan State Capitol">\n          Michigan State Capitol\n         </a>\n         in Lansing\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg/220px-Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg/330px-Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg/440px-Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_State_Capitol_Muses.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Michigan State Capitol Muses\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg/170px-712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg/255px-712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg/340px-712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:712_michigan_hofj_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Supreme_Court" title="Michigan Supreme Court">\n          Michigan Supreme Court\n         </a>\n         at the Hall of Justice\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="State_government">\n        State government\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Michigan" title="Government of Michigan">\n        Government of Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is governed as a republic, with three\n       <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">\n        branches of government\n       </a>\n       : the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">\n        executive branch\n       </a>\n       consisting of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Michigan" title="Governor of Michigan">\n        Governor of Michigan\n       </a>\n       and the other independently elected constitutional officers; the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">\n        legislative branch\n       </a>\n       consisting of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_State_House_of_Representatives" title="Michigan State House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Senate" title="Michigan Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       ; and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">\n        judicial branch\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_Constitution" title="Michigan Constitution">\n        Michigan Constitution\n       </a>\n       allows for the direct participation of the electorate by statutory\n       <a href="/wiki/Initiative" title="Initiative">\n        initiative\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">\n        referendum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Recall_election" title="Recall election">\n        recall\n       </a>\n       , and constitutional initiative and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">\n        referral\n       </a>\n       (Article II, \xc2\xa7 9,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       defined as "the power to propose laws and to enact and reject laws, called the initiative, and the power to approve or reject laws enacted by the legislature, called the referendum. The power of initiative extends only to laws which the legislature may enact under this constitution").\n       <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States" title="List of capitals in the United States">\n        state capital\n       </a>\n       and is home to all three branches of state government.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Michigan" title="Governor of Michigan">\n        governor\n       </a>\n       and the other state constitutional officers serve four-year terms and may be re-elected only once. The current governor is\n       <a href="/wiki/Rick_Snyder" title="Rick Snyder">\n        Rick Snyder\n       </a>\n       . Michigan has two official\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_Governor%27s_Residence" title="Michigan Governor\'s Residence">\n        Governor\'s Residences\n       </a>\n       ; one is in Lansing, and the other is at\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Island" title="Mackinac Island">\n        Mackinac Island\n       </a>\n       . The other constitutionally elected executive officers are the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Michigan" title="Lieutenant Governor of Michigan">\n        lieutenant governor\n       </a>\n       , who is elected on a joint ticket with the governor, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Michigan" title="Secretary of State of Michigan">\n        secretary of state\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Michigan" title="Attorney General of Michigan">\n        attorney general\n       </a>\n       . The lieutenant governor presides over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Senate" title="Michigan Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       , but only voting when ties occur, and is also a member of the cabinet. The secretary of state is the chief elections officer and is charged with running many licensure programs including motor vehicles, all of which are done through the branch offices of the secretary of state.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Legislature" title="Michigan Legislature">\n        Michigan Legislature\n       </a>\n       consists of a 38-member Senate and 110-member\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_State_House_of_Representatives" title="Michigan State House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       . Members of both houses of the legislature are elected through\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" title="First past the post">\n        first past the post\n       </a>\n       elections by single-member electoral districts of near-equal population that often have boundaries which coincide with county and municipal lines. Senators serve four-year terms concurrent to those of the governor, while representatives serve two-year terms. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Capitol" title="Michigan State Capitol">\n        Michigan State Capitol\n       </a>\n       was dedicated in 1879 and has hosted the executive and legislative branches of the state ever since.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Michigan judiciary consists of two courts with primary jurisdiction (the Circuit Courts and the District Courts), one intermediate level appellate court (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Court_of_Appeals" title="Michigan Court of Appeals">\n        Michigan Court of Appeals\n       </a>\n       ), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Supreme_Court" title="Michigan Supreme Court">\n        Michigan Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       . There are several administrative courts and specialized courts. District courts are trial courts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Limited_jurisdiction" title="Limited jurisdiction">\n        limited jurisdiction\n       </a>\n       , handling most traffic violations, small claims,\n       <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">\n        misdemeanors\n       </a>\n       , and civil suits where the amount contended is below $25,000. District courts are often responsible for handling the preliminary examination and for setting bail in felony cases. District court judges are elected to terms of six years. In a few locations, municipal courts have been retained to the exclusion of the establishment of district courts. There are 57 circuit courts in the State of Michigan, which have\n       <a href="/wiki/Original_jurisdiction" title="Original jurisdiction">\n        original jurisdiction\n       </a>\n       over all civil suits where the amount contended in the case exceeds $25,000 and all criminal cases involving\n       <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">\n        felonies\n       </a>\n       . Circuit courts are also the only trial courts in the State of Michigan which possess the power to issue\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equitable_remedies" title="Equitable remedies">\n        equitable remedies\n       </a>\n       . Circuit courts have\n       <a href="/wiki/Appellate_jurisdiction" title="Appellate jurisdiction">\n        appellate jurisdiction\n       </a>\n       from district and municipal courts, as well as from decisions and decrees of state agencies. Most counties have their own circuit court, but sparsely populated counties often share them. Circuit court judges are elected to terms of six years. State appellate court judges are elected to terms of six years, but vacancies are filled by an appointment by the governor. There are four divisions of the Court of Appeals, being located in Detroit,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids" title="Grand Rapids">\n        Grand Rapids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lansing" title="Lansing">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marquette,_Michigan" title="Marquette, Michigan">\n        Marquette\n       </a>\n       . Cases are heard by the Court of Appeals by panels of three judges, who examine the application of the law and not the facts of the case, unless there has been grievous error pertaining to questions of fact. The Michigan Supreme Court consists of seven members who are elected on non-partisan ballots for staggered eight-year terms. The Supreme Court has original jurisdiction only in narrow circumstances, but holds appellate jurisdiction over the entire state judicial system.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law">\n        Law\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Michigan" title="Law of Michigan">\n        Law of Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan has had four\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_Constitution" title="Michigan Constitution">\n        constitutions\n       </a>\n       , the first of which was ratified on October 5 and 6, 1835.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There were also constitutions from 1850 and 1908, in addition to the current constitution from 1963. The current document has a preamble, 11\xc2\xa0articles, and one section consisting of a schedule and temporary provisions. Michigan, like every U.S. state except\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">\n        common law\n       </a>\n       legal system.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Michigan" title="Elections in Michigan">\n        Elections in Michigan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Michigan" title="Political party strength in Michigan">\n        Political party strength in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RickSnyder.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="860" data-file-width="948" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/RickSnyder.jpg/220px-RickSnyder.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/RickSnyder.jpg/330px-RickSnyder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/RickSnyder.jpg/440px-RickSnyder.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RickSnyder.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Michigan" title="Governor of Michigan">\n          Michigan Governor\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Rick_Snyder" title="Rick Snyder">\n          Rick Snyder\n         </a>\n         (R) (2011\xe2\x80\x93present)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:307px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan,_2016.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="2904" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg/305px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg/458px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg/610px-United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" width="305"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_Michigan,_2016.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treemap" title="Treemap">\n          Treemap\n         </a>\n         of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Voters in the state elect candidates from both major parties. Economic issues are important in Michigan elections.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The three-term Republican Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Engler" title="John Engler">\n        John Engler\n       </a>\n       (1991\xe2\x80\x932003) preceded the former two-term Democratic Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Granholm" title="Jennifer Granholm">\n        Jennifer Granholm\n       </a>\n       (2003\xe2\x80\x932011). The state has elected successive Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Attorney_General" title="Michigan Attorney General">\n        attorneys general\n       </a>\n       twice since 2003. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican Party\n       </a>\n       currently holds a majority in both the House and Senate of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Legislature" title="Michigan Legislature">\n        Michigan Legislature\n       </a>\n       . Michigan supported the election of Republican Presidents\n       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">\n        Ronald Reagan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">\n        George H. W. Bush\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">\n        Donald Trump\n       </a>\n       . The current Governor Rick Snyder (2011\xe2\x80\x93present) is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In contrast, the state supported Democratic candidates in each presidential election from 1992 to 2012. In 2012,\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       carried the state over\n       <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">\n        Mitt Romney\n       </a>\n       , winning Michigan\'s 17 electoral votes with 54% of the vote. Michigan\'s two U.S. Senators are both Democrats, while Republicans hold nine of the state\'s fourteen\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_delegations_from_Michigan" title="United States congressional delegations from Michigan">\n        US House\n       </a>\n       seats.
