Michigan\'s current senior U.S. Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Stabenow" title="Debbie Stabenow">\n        Debbie Stabenow\n       </a>\n       , a Democrat, has served since 2001 after narrowly beating former Republican U.S. Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Abraham" title="Spencer Abraham">\n        Spencer Abraham\n       </a>\n       in the 2000 elections. Democratic U.S. Senator\n       <a href="/wiki/Gary_Peters_(politician)" title="Gary Peters (politician)">\n        Gary Peters\n       </a>\n       was elected in 2014, beating former Republican Michigan Secretary of State\n       <a href="/wiki/Terri_Lynn_Land" title="Terri Lynn Land">\n        Terri Lynn Land\n       </a>\n       . Congressman\n       <a href="/wiki/Fred_Upton" title="Fred Upton">\n        Fred Upton\n       </a>\n       , a Republican, serves as Chairman of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_Energy_and_Commerce" title="United States House Committee on Energy and Commerce">\n        US House Committee on Energy and Commerce\n       </a>\n       . Congresswoman\n       <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Dingell" title="Debbie Dingell">\n        Debbie Dingell\n       </a>\n       , a Democrat, became the first person to succeed a living spouse when she replaced former\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dean_of_the_House_of_Representatives" title="Dean of the House of Representatives">\n        Dean of the House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Dingell" title="John Dingell">\n        John Dingell\n       </a>\n       in 2015.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Republican strongholds of the state include rural areas of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Michigan" title="Western Michigan">\n        Western\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Michigan" title="North Michigan">\n        Northern Michigan\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids" title="Grand Rapids">\n        Grand Rapids\n       </a>\n       metropolitan area, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Livingston_County,_Michigan" title="Livingston County, Michigan">\n        Livingston County\n       </a>\n       . Areas of Democratic strength include\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_County,_Michigan" title="Wayne County, Michigan">\n        Wayne County\n       </a>\n       , home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">\n        Detroit\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Washtenaw_County,_Michigan" title="Washtenaw County, Michigan">\n        Washtenaw County\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor" title="Ann Arbor">\n        Ann Arbor\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Ingham_County,_Michigan" title="Ingham County, Michigan">\n        Ingham County\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lansing" title="Lansing">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       ), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Genesee_County,_Michigan" title="Genesee County, Michigan">\n        Genesee County\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">\n        Flint\n       </a>\n       ). Much of suburban Detroit\xe2\x80\x94which includes parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_County,_Michigan" title="Oakland County, Michigan">\n        Oakland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Macomb_County,_Michigan" title="Macomb County, Michigan">\n        Macomb\n       </a>\n       , and Wayne counties\xe2\x80\x94is politically competitive between the two parties.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Historically, the first county-level meeting of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republican Party\n       </a>\n       took place in\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson,_Michigan" title="Jackson, Michigan">\n        Jackson\n       </a>\n       on July 6, 1854,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the party thereafter dominated Michigan until the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       . In the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1912" title="United States presidential election, 1912">\n        1912 election\n       </a>\n       , Michigan was one of the six states to support progressive Republican and third-party candidate\n       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">\n        Theodore Roosevelt\n       </a>\n       for president after he lost the Republican nomination to\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">\n        William Howard Taft\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan remained fairly reliably Republican at the presidential level for much of the 20th century. It was part of Greater New England, the northern tier of states settled chiefly by migrants from New England who carried their culture with them. The state was one of only a handful to back\n       <a href="/wiki/Wendell_Willkie" title="Wendell Willkie">\n        Wendell Willkie\n       </a>\n       over\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_Roosevelt" title="Franklin Roosevelt">\n        Franklin Roosevelt\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1940" title="United States presidential election, 1940">\n        1940\n       </a>\n       , and supported\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey" title="Thomas E. Dewey">\n        Thomas E. Dewey\n       </a>\n       in his losing bid against\n       <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">\n        Harry S. Truman\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1948" title="United States presidential election, 1948">\n        1948\n       </a>\n       . Michigan went to the Democrats in presidential elections during the 1960s, and voted for the Republican candidate in every election from 1972 to 1988. Between 1992 and 2012 it supported the Democrats; early on in 2016, it was pegged as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">\n        swing state\n       </a>\n       , and was won very narrowly by the G.O.P. candidate,\n       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">\n        Donald Trump\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan was the home of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">\n        Gerald Ford\n       </a>\n       , the 38th President of the United States. He was born in Nebraska and moved as an infant to Grand Rapids and grew up there.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ford-Nebraska_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ford-Nebraska-39">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford_Museum" title="Gerald R. Ford Museum">\n        Gerald R. Ford Museum\n       </a>\n       is located in Grand Rapids, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford_Presidential_Library" title="Gerald R. Ford Presidential Library">\n        Gerald R. Ford Presidential Library\n       </a>\n       is located on the campus of his alma mater, the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       in Ann Arbor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1846 Michigan became the first state in the Union, as well as the first English-speaking government in the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Michigan" title="Capital punishment in Michigan">\n        to abolish the death penalty\n       </a>\n       . Historian\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Chardavoyne" title="David Chardavoyne">\n        David Chardavoyne\n       </a>\n       has suggested that the movement to abolish capital punishment in Michigan grew as a result of enmity toward the state\'s neighbor, Canada. Under British rule, it made public executions a regular practice.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan has recognized and performed same-sex marriages since June 26, 2015, following the Supreme Court ruling in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Obergefell_v._Hodges" title="Obergefell v. Hodges">\n         Obergefell v. Hodges\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Previously, such unions were prohibited under\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Proposal_04-2" title="Michigan Proposal 04-2">\n        a 2004 state constitutional amendment\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan has approved plans to expand\n       <a href="/wiki/Medicaid" title="Medicaid">\n        Medicaid\n       </a>\n       coverage in 2014 to adults with incomes up to 133% of the federal poverty level (approximately $15,500 for a single adult in 2014).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">\n        Administrative divisions\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_welcome.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1087" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Michigan_welcome.jpg/220px-Michigan_welcome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Michigan_welcome.jpg/330px-Michigan_welcome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Michigan_welcome.jpg/440px-Michigan_welcome.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_welcome.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Michigan welcome sign\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Michigan" title="Administrative divisions of Michigan">\n        Administrative divisions of Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_county_seats" title="List of Michigan county seats">\n        List of Michigan county seats\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Michigan" title="List of counties in Michigan">\n        List of counties in Michigan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Michigan_(by_population)" title="List of municipalities in Michigan (by population)">\n        List of municipalities in Michigan (by population)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       State government is decentralized among three tiers\xe2\x80\x94statewide, county and township. Counties are administrative divisions of the state, and townships are administrative divisions of a county. Both of them exercise state government authority, localized to meet the particular needs of their jurisdictions, as provided by state law. There are 83\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Michigan" title="List of counties in Michigan">\n        counties in Michigan\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cities,\n       <a href="/wiki/State_university_system" title="State university system">\n        state universities\n       </a>\n       , and villages are vested with\n       <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">\n        home rule\n       </a>\n       powers of varying degrees. Home rule cities can generally do anything that is not prohibited by law. The fifteen state universities have broad power and can do anything within the parameters of their status as educational institutions that is not prohibited by the state constitution. Villages, by contrast, have limited home rule and are not completely autonomous from the county and township in which they are located.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are two types of\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_township" title="Civil township">\n        township\n       </a>\n       in Michigan:\n       <i>\n        general law\n       </i>\n       township and\n       <i>\n        charter\n       </i>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Charter_township" title="Charter township">\n        Charter township\n       </a>\n       status was created by the Legislature in 1947 and grants additional powers and stream-lined administration in order to provide greater protection against annexation by a city. As of April 2001, there were 127 charter townships in Michigan. In general, charter townships have many of the same powers as a city but without the same level of obligations. For example, a charter township can have its own fire department, water and sewer department, police department, and so on\xe2\x80\x94just like a city\xe2\x80\x94but it is not\n       <i>\n        required\n       </i>\n       to have those things, whereas cities\n       <i>\n        must\n       </i>\n       provide those services. Charter townships can opt to use county-wide services instead, such as deputies from the county sheriff\'s office instead of a home-based force of ordinance officers.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Michigan" title="Geography of Michigan">\n        Geography of Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Michigan" title="Protected areas of Michigan">\n        Protected areas of Michigan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_state_parks" title="List of Michigan state parks">\n        List of Michigan state parks\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="">\n        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MarquetteParkMI.png" title="Marquette Park on Mackinac Island">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="1744" data-file-width="6448" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/MarquetteParkMI.png/900px-MarquetteParkMI.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/MarquetteParkMI.png/1350px-MarquetteParkMI.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/MarquetteParkMI.png/1800px-MarquetteParkMI.png 2x" width="900"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a href="/wiki/File:MarquetteParkMI.png" title="File:MarquetteParkMI.png">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Marquette_Park_(Mackinac_Island)" title="Marquette Park (Mackinac Island)">\n          Marquette Park\n         </a>\n         on\n         <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Island" title="Mackinac Island">\n          Mackinac Island\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan consists of two peninsulas that lie between 82\xc2\xb030\' to about 90\xc2\xb030\' west longitude, and are separated by the Straits of Mackinac. The\n       <a href="/wiki/45th_parallel_north" title="45th parallel north">\n        45th parallel north\n       </a>\n       runs through the state\xe2\x80\x94marked by highway signs and the Polar-Equator Trail\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       \xe2\x80\x94along a line including\n       <a href="/wiki/Mission_Point_Light" title="Mission Point Light">\n        Mission Point Light\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Traverse_City,_Michigan" title="Traverse City, Michigan">\n        Traverse City\n       </a>\n       , the towns of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gaylord,_Michigan" title="Gaylord, Michigan">\n        Gaylord\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpena,_Michigan" title="Alpena, Michigan">\n        Alpena\n       </a>\n       in the Lower Peninsula and\n       <a href="/wiki/Menominee,_Michigan" title="Menominee, Michigan">\n        Menominee\n       </a>\n       in the Upper Peninsula. With the exception of two small areas that are drained by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">\n        Mississippi River\n       </a>\n       by way of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_River" title="Wisconsin River">\n        Wisconsin River\n       </a>\n       in the Upper Peninsula and by way of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kankakee_River" title="Kankakee River">\n        Kankakee\n       </a>\n       -\n       <a href="/wiki/Illinois_River" title="Illinois River">\n        Illinois River\n       </a>\n       in the Lower Peninsula, Michigan is drained by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       -\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">\n        St. Lawrence\n       </a>\n       watershed and is the only state with the majority of its land thus drained.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2142" data-file-width="2955" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg/170px-Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg/255px-Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg/340px-Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sleeping_Bear_Dunes.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleeping_Bear_Dunes" title="Sleeping Bear Dunes">\n          Sleeping Bear Dunes\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Great Lakes that border Michigan from east to west are\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">\n        Lake Erie\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">\n        Lake Huron\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">\n        Lake Michigan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">\n        Lake Superior\n       </a>\n       . It has more\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Public_golf_courses&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Public golf courses (page does not exist)">\n        public golf courses\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Registered_boats&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Registered boats (page does not exist)">\n        registered boats\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">\n        lighthouses\n       </a>\n       than any other state. The state is bounded on the south by the states of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">\n        Indiana\n       </a>\n       , sharing land and water boundaries with both. Michigan\'s western boundaries are almost entirely water boundaries, from south to north, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">\n        Illinois\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">\n        Wisconsin\n       </a>\n       in Lake Michigan; then a land boundary with Wisconsin and the Upper Peninsula, that is principally demarcated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Menominee_River" title="Menominee River">\n        Menominee\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montreal_River_(Wisconsin-Michigan)" title="Montreal River (Wisconsin-Michigan)">\n        Montreal Rivers\n       </a>\n       ; then water boundaries again, in Lake Superior, with Wisconsin and\n       <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">\n        Minnesota\n       </a>\n       to the west, capped around by the Canadian province of Ontario to the north and east.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg/220px-Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg/330px-Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg/440px-Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tahquamenon_falls_upper.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tahquamenon_Falls" title="Tahquamenon Falls">\n          Tahquamenon Falls\n         </a>\n         in the\n         <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Upper Peninsula of Michigan">\n          Upper Peninsula\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The heavily forested\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Upper Peninsula of Michigan">\n        Upper Peninsula\n       </a>\n       is relatively mountainous in the west. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Porcupine_Mountains" title="Porcupine Mountains">\n        Porcupine Mountains\n       </a>\n       , which are part of one of the oldest mountain chains in the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       rise to an altitude of almost 2,000 feet (610\xc2\xa0m) above sea level and form the watershed between the streams flowing into Lake Superior and Lake Michigan. The surface on either side of this range is rugged. The state\'s highest point, in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Huron_Mountains" title="Huron Mountains">\n        Huron Mountains\n       </a>\n       northwest of Marquette, is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Arvon" title="Mount Arvon">\n        Mount Arvon\n       </a>\n       at 1,979 feet (603\xc2\xa0m). The peninsula is as large as Connecticut, Delaware, Massachusetts, and Rhode Island combined but has fewer than 330,000 inhabitants. They are sometimes called "Yoopers" (from "U.P.\'ers"), and their speech (the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yooper_dialect" title="Yooper dialect">\n        Yooper dialect\n       </a>\n       ") has been heavily influenced by the numerous\n       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">\n        Scandinavian\n       </a>\n       and Canadian immigrants who settled the area during the lumbering and\n       <a href="/wiki/Copper_mining_in_Michigan" title="Copper mining in Michigan">\n        mining boom\n       </a>\n       of the late 19th century.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pointe_Mouillee.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1202" data-file-width="1500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Pointe_Mouillee.jpg/220px-Pointe_Mouillee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Pointe_Mouillee.jpg/330px-Pointe_Mouillee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Pointe_Mouillee.jpg/440px-Pointe_Mouillee.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pointe_Mouillee.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Pointe Mouillee State Game Area\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Lower Peninsula of Michigan">\n        Lower Peninsula\n       </a>\n       is shaped like a mitten and many residents hold up a hand to depict where they are from.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keilman20111209_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-keilman20111209-47">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is 277 miles (446\xc2\xa0km) long from north to south and 195 miles (314\xc2\xa0km) from east to west and occupies nearly two-thirds of the state\'s land area. The surface of the peninsula is generally level, broken by conical hills and glacial\n       <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">\n        moraines\n       </a>\n       usually not more than a few hundred feet tall. It is divided by a low water divide running north and south. The larger portion of the state is on the west of this and gradually slopes toward Lake Michigan. The highest point in the Lower Peninsula is either Briar Hill at 1,705 feet (520\xc2\xa0m), or one of several points nearby in the vicinity of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cadillac,_Michigan" title="Cadillac, Michigan">\n        Cadillac\n       </a>\n       . The lowest point is the surface of Lake Erie at 571 feet (174\xc2\xa0m).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The geographic orientation of Michigan\'s peninsulas makes for a long distance between the ends of the state.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ironwood,_Michigan" title="Ironwood, Michigan">\n        Ironwood\n       </a>\n       , in the far western Upper Peninsula, lies 630 highway miles (1,015\xc2\xa0km) from\n       <a href="/wiki/Lambertville,_Michigan" title="Lambertville, Michigan">\n        Lambertville\n       </a>\n       in the Lower Peninsula\'s southeastern corner. The geographic isolation of the Upper Peninsula from Michigan\'s political and population centers makes the U.P. culturally and economically distinct. Occasionally U.P. residents have called for\n       <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">\n        secession\n       </a>\n       from Michigan and establishment as a new state to be called "\n       <a href="/wiki/Superior_(proposed_U.S._state)" title="Superior (proposed U.S. state)">\n        Superior\n       </a>\n       ".\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A feature of Michigan that gives it the distinct shape of a mitten is\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Thumb" title="The Thumb">\n        the Thumb\n       </a>\n       . This peninsula projects out into Lake Huron and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saginaw_Bay" title="Saginaw Bay">\n        Saginaw Bay\n       </a>\n       . The geography of the Thumb is mainly flat with a few rolling hills. Other peninsulas of Michigan include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Keweenaw_Peninsula" title="Keweenaw Peninsula">\n        Keweenaw Peninsula\n       </a>\n       , making up the\n       <a href="/wiki/Copper_Country" title="Copper Country">\n        Copper Country\n       </a>\n       region of the state. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Leelanau_County,_Michigan" title="Leelanau County, Michigan">\n        Leelanau Peninsula\n       </a>\n       lies in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan" title="Northern Michigan">\n        Northern Lower Michigan\n       </a>\n       region.\n       <i>\n        See Also\n        <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States#Michigan" title="List of regions of the United States">\n         Michigan Regions\n        </a>\n       </i>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="500" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg/220px-Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg/330px-Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg/440px-Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Little_Sable_Light_Point_Light_Station_-_Michigan.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Little_Sable_Point_Light" title="Little Sable Point Light">\n          Little Sable Point Light\n         </a>\n         south of\n         <a href="/wiki/Pentwater,_Michigan" title="Pentwater, Michigan">\n          Pentwater\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Numerous lakes and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">\n        marshes\n       </a>\n       mark both peninsulas, and the coast is much indented. Keweenaw Bay,\n       <a href="/wiki/Whitefish_Bay" title="Whitefish Bay">\n        Whitefish Bay\n       </a>\n       , and the Big and\n       <a href="/wiki/Little_Bay_de_Noc" title="Little Bay de Noc">\n        Little\n       </a>\n       Bays De Noc are the principal indentations on the Upper Peninsula. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Traverse_Bay" title="Grand Traverse Bay">\n        Grand\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Little_Traverse_Bay" title="Little Traverse Bay">\n        Little Traverse\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay_(Michigan)" title="Thunder Bay (Michigan)">\n        Thunder\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saginaw_Bay" title="Saginaw Bay">\n        Saginaw\n       </a>\n       bays indent the Lower Peninsula. Michigan has the second longest shoreline of any state\xe2\x80\x943,288 miles (5,292\xc2\xa0km),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       including 1,056 miles (1,699\xc2\xa0km) of island shoreline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="612" data-file-width="741" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Michigan.svg/220px-Michigan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Michigan.svg/330px-Michigan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Michigan.svg/440px-Michigan.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Michigan map, including territorial waters\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The state has\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islands_of_Michigan" title="Islands of Michigan">\n        numerous large islands\n       </a>\n       , the principal ones being the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Manitou_Island" title="North Manitou Island">\n        North Manitou\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Manitou_Island" title="North Manitou Island">\n        South Manitou\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Island_(Lake_Michigan)" title="Beaver Island (Lake Michigan)">\n        Beaver\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fox_Islands_(Michigan)" title="Fox Islands (Michigan)">\n        Fox\n       </a>\n       groups in Lake Michigan;\n       <a href="/wiki/Isle_Royale" title="Isle Royale">\n        Isle Royale\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Island_(Michigan)" title="Grand Island (Michigan)">\n        Grande Isle\n       </a>\n       in Lake Superior; Marquette,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bois_Blanc_Island_(Michigan)" title="Bois Blanc Island (Michigan)">\n        Bois Blanc\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Island" title="Mackinac Island">\n        Mackinac\n       </a>\n       islands in Lake Huron; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Neebish_Island" title="Neebish Island">\n        Neebish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Island_(Michigan)" title="Sugar Island (Michigan)">\n        Sugar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drummond_Island" title="Drummond Island">\n        Drummond\n       </a>\n       islands in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Marys_River_(Michigan-Ontario)" title="St. Marys River (Michigan-Ontario)">\n        St. Mary\'s River\n       </a>\n       . Michigan has about 150\n       <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">\n        lighthouses\n       </a>\n       , the most of any U.S. state. The first lighthouses in Michigan were built between 1818 and 1822. They were built to project light at night and to serve as a landmark during the day to safely guide the passenger ships and freighters traveling the Great Lakes. See\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lighthouses_in_the_United_States#Michigan" title="Lighthouses in the United States">\n        Lighthouses in the United States\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_rivers" title="List of Michigan rivers">\n        state\'s rivers\n       </a>\n       are generally small, short and shallow, and few are navigable. The principal ones include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n        Detroit River\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Marys_River_(Michigan-Ontario)" title="St. Marys River (Michigan-Ontario)">\n        St. Marys River\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Clair_River" title="St. Clair River">\n        St. Clair River\n       </a>\n       which connect the Great Lakes; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Au_Sable_River_(Michigan)" title="Au Sable River (Michigan)">\n        Au Sable\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cheboygan_River" title="Cheboygan River">\n        Cheboygan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saginaw_River" title="Saginaw River">\n        Saginaw\n       </a>\n       , which flow into Lake Huron; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontonagon_River" title="Ontonagon River">\n        Ontonagon\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tahquamenon_River" title="Tahquamenon River">\n        Tahquamenon\n       </a>\n       , which flow into Lake Superior; and the\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph_River_(Lake_Michigan)" title="St. Joseph River (Lake Michigan)">\n        St. Joseph\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kalamazoo_River" title="Kalamazoo River">\n        Kalamazoo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_River_(Michigan)" title="Grand River (Michigan)">\n        Grand\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Muskegon_River" title="Muskegon River">\n        Muskegon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Manistee_River" title="Manistee River">\n        Manistee\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Escanaba_River" title="Escanaba River">\n        Escanaba\n       </a>\n       , which flow into Lake Michigan. The state has 11,037 inland lakes\xe2\x80\x94totaling 1,305 square miles (3,380\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of inland water\xe2\x80\x94in addition to 38,575 square miles (99,910\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of Great Lakes waters. No point in Michigan is more than six miles (9.7\xc2\xa0km) from an inland lake or more than 85 miles (137\xc2\xa0km) from one of the Great Lakes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state is home to a number of areas maintained by the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">\n        National Park Service\n       </a>\n       including:\n       <a href="/wiki/Isle_Royale_National_Park" title="Isle Royale National Park">\n        Isle Royale National Park\n       </a>\n       , located in Lake Superior, about 30 miles (48\xc2\xa0km) southeast of Thunder Bay, Ontario. Other national\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protected_areas" title="Protected areas">\n        protected areas\n       </a>\n       in the state include:\n       <a href="/wiki/Keweenaw_National_Historical_Park" title="Keweenaw National Historical Park">\n        Keweenaw National Historical Park\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pictured_Rocks_National_Lakeshore" title="Pictured Rocks National Lakeshore">\n        Pictured Rocks National Lakeshore\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Bear_Dunes_National_Lakeshore" title="Sleeping Bear Dunes National Lakeshore">\n        Sleeping Bear Dunes National Lakeshore\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huron_National_Forest" title="Huron National Forest">\n        Huron National Forest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manistee_National_Forest" title="Manistee National Forest">\n        Manistee National Forest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hiawatha_National_Forest" title="Hiawatha National Forest">\n        Hiawatha National Forest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_National_Forest" title="Ottawa National Forest">\n        Ottawa National Forest\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Father_Marquette_National_Memorial" title="Father Marquette National Memorial">\n        Father Marquette National Memorial\n       </a>\n       . The largest section of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Country_National_Scenic_Trail" title="North Country National Scenic Trail">\n        North Country National Scenic Trail\n       </a>\n       passes through Michigan.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With 78\n       <a href="/wiki/State_park" title="State park">\n        state parks\n       </a>\n       , 19 state recreation areas, and 6\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_forests" title="State forests">\n        state forests\n       </a>\n       , Michigan has the largest state park and\n       <a href="/wiki/State_forest" title="State forest">\n        state forest\n       </a>\n       system of any state. These parks and forests include\n       <a href="/wiki/Holland_State_Park" title="Holland State Park">\n        Holland State Park\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Island_State_Park" title="Mackinac Island State Park">\n        Mackinac Island State Park\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Au_Sable_State_Forest" title="Au Sable State Forest">\n        Au Sable State Forest\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinaw_State_Forest" title="Mackinaw State Forest">\n        Mackinaw State Forest\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MI_koppen.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1512" data-file-width="1080" height="420" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MI_koppen.svg/300px-MI_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MI_koppen.svg/450px-MI_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/MI_koppen.svg/600px-MI_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MI_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         K\xc3\xb6ppen climate types in Michigan\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="infobox" style="width: 19.5em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right">\n              <span style="font-size:80%">\n               \xe2\x88\x922\n              </span>\n             </div>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <div style="width:1.6em;height:17em;position:relative;padding:0;margin:0">\n             <div style="height:0em;bottom:2em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #abc;padding:0;margin:0">\n             </div>\n             <div style="background:#ace;position:absolute;bottom:2em;left:.2em;width:1.2em;height:0.9906em;overflow:hidden">\n             </div>\n             <div style="color:blue;position:absolute;bottom:.5em;left:0;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:center">\n              <span style="font-size:70%">\n               50\n              </span>\n             </div>\n             <div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">\n             </div>\n             <div style="overflow:hidden;background:#e44;position:absolute;left:.2em;width:1.2em;bottom:6.44em;height:1.3333333333333em;">\n             </div>\n             <div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:7.7733333333333em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right">\n              <span style="font-size:80%">\n               \xe2\x88\x921\n              </span>\n             </div>\n             <div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:4.94em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right">\n              <span style="font-size:80%">\n               \xe2\x88\x928\n              </span>\n             </div>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: red">\n            Average max. and min. temperatures in \xc2\xb0C\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px; text-align: left; line-height: 1.5em; color: blue">\n            Precipitation totals in mm\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Michigan has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n        continental climate\n       </a>\n       , although there are two distinct regions. The southern and central parts of the Lower Peninsula (south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Saginaw_Bay" title="Saginaw Bay">\n        Saginaw Bay\n       </a>\n       and from the Grand Rapids area southward) have a warmer climate (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Dfa\n       </i>\n       ) with hot summers and cold winters. The northern part of Lower Peninsula and the entire Upper Peninsula has a more severe climate (K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       <i>\n        Dfb\n       </i>\n       ), with warm, but shorter summers and longer, cold to very cold winters. Some parts of the state average high temperatures below freezing from December through February, and into early March in the far northern parts. During the winter through the middle of February the state is frequently subjected to heavy\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">\n        lake-effect snow\n       </a>\n       . The state averages from 30\xe2\x80\x9340 inches (76\xe2\x80\x93102\xc2\xa0cm) of precipitation annually, however some areas in the northern lower peninsula and the upper peninsula average almost 160" of snowfall per year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s highest recorded temperature is 112\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (44\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) at\n       <a href="/wiki/Mio,_Michigan" title="Mio, Michigan">\n        Mio\n       </a>\n       on July 13, 1936, and the coldest recorded temperature is \xe2\x88\x9251\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9246\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) at\n       <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt,_Michigan" title="Vanderbilt, Michigan">\n        Vanderbilt\n       </a>\n       on February 9, 1934.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-netstate_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-netstate-54">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The entire state averages 30 days of thunderstorm activity per year. These can be severe, especially in the southern part of the state. The state averages 17\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">\n        tornadoes\n       </a>\n       per year, which are more common in the extreme southern portion of the state. Portions of the southern border have been almost as vulnerable historically as states further west and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">\n        Tornado Alley\n       </a>\n       . For this reason, many communities in the very southern portions of the state are equipped with tornado sirens to warn residents of approaching tornadoes. Farther north, in Central Michigan, Northern Michigan, and the Upper Peninsula, tornadoes are rare.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thunderstorm_hazards_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Thunderstorm_hazards-56">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">\n        Geology\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The geological formation of the state is greatly varied, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Basin" title="Michigan Basin">\n        Michigan Basin\n       </a>\n       being the most major formation. Primary boulders are found over the entire surface of the Upper Peninsula (being principally of primitive origin), while Secondary deposits cover the entire Lower Peninsula. The Upper Peninsula exhibits Lower\n       <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">\n        Silurian\n       </a>\n       sandstones, limestones, copper and iron bearing rocks, corresponding to the Huronian system of\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       . The central portion of the Lower Peninsula contains coal measures and rocks of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvanian_(geology)" title="Pennsylvanian (geology)">\n        Pennsylvanian\n       </a>\n       period.\n       <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">\n        Devonian\n       </a>\n       and sub-Carboniferous deposits are scattered over the entire state.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan rarely experiences\n       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">\n        earthquakes\n       </a>\n       , thus far mostly smaller ones that do not cause significant damage. A 4.6-magnitude earthquake struck in August 1947. More recently, a 4.2-magnitude earthquake occurred on Saturday, May 2, 2015, shortly after noon, about 5 miles south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Galesburg,_Michigan" title="Galesburg, Michigan">\n        Galesburg, Michigan\n       </a>\n       (9 miles southeast of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalamazoo" title="Kalamazoo">\n        Kalamazoo\n       </a>\n       ) in central Michigan, about 140 miles west of Detroit, according to the Colorado-based\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Geological_Survey" title="U.S. Geological Survey">\n        U.S. Geological Survey\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Earthquake_Information_Center" title="National Earthquake Information Center">\n        National Earthquake Information Center\n       </a>\n       . No major damage or injuries were reported, according to Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Rick_Snyder" title="Rick Snyder">\n        Rick Snyder\n       </a>\n       \'s office.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n  </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population">\n        Population\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       estimates that the population of Michigan was 9,928,300 on July 1, 2016, an increase of 0.45% from 9,883,635 recorded at the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_60-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-60">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">\n        center of population\n       </a>\n       of Michigan is located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Shiawassee_County,_Michigan" title="Shiawassee County, Michigan">\n        Shiawassee County\n       </a>\n       , in the southeastern corner of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_township" title="Civil township">\n        civil township\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bennington_Township,_MI" title="Bennington Township, MI">\n        Bennington\n       </a>\n       , which is located northwest of the village of\n       <a href="/wiki/Morrice,_Michigan" title="Morrice, Michigan">\n        Morrice\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of the 2010\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">\n        American Community Survey\n       </a>\n       for the U.S. Census, the state had a foreign-born population of 592,212, or 6.0% of the total. Michigan has the largest\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_American" title="Dutch American">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finnish_American" title="Finnish American">\n        Finnish\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_American" title="Macedonian American">\n        Macedonian\n       </a>\n       populations in the United States.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 Census\n       </a>\n       reported:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">\n         White American\n        </a>\n        : 78.9% (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">\n         Non-Hispanic Whites\n        </a>\n        : 76.6%,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Hispanic" title="White Hispanic">\n         White Hispanic\n        </a>\n        : 2.3%)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Black or\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">\n         African American\n        </a>\n        : 14.2%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n         American Indian\n        </a>\n        : 0.6%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">\n         Asian American\n        </a>\n        : 2.4%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">\n         Pacific Islander\n        </a>\n        : &lt;0.1%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Some other race: 1.5%\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n         Multiracial\n        </a>\n        : 2.3%\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In the same year\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">\n        Hispanics or Latinos\n       </a>\n       (of any race) made up 4.4% of the population.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n       <caption>\n        <b>\n         Michigan Racial Breakdown of Population\n title="Polish American">\n          Polish\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         8.4%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_ethnicity" title="American ethnicity">\n          American\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         6.0%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_American" title="Dutch American">\n          Dutch\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">\n          Italian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4.6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/French_Americans" title="French Americans">\n          French\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4.2%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_American" title="Scottish American">\n          Scottish\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2.1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_American" title="Arab American">\n          Arab\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.8%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French-Canadian_Americans" title="French-Canadian Americans">\n          French-Canadian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.7%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_American" title="Swedish American">\n          Swedish\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.4%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_American" title="Hungarian American">\n          Hungarian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.9%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_American" title="Norwegian American">\n          Norwegian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.8%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_American" title="Russian American">\n          Russian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.8%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_American" title="Scotch-Irish American">\n          Scotch-Irish\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.7%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MichiganAncestry.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="605" data-file-width="559" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/MichiganAncestry.svg/220px-MichiganAncestry.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/MichiganAncestry.svg/330px-MichiganAncestry.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/MichiganAncestry.svg/440px-MichiganAncestry.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MichiganAncestry.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map showing the largest ancestry group in each county (2008)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The large majority of Michigan\'s population is Caucasian.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_American" title="European American">\n        Americans of European descent\n       </a>\n       live throughout Michigan and most of Metro Detroit. Large European American groups include those of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">\n        German\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_American" title="British American">\n        British\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">\n        Irish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">\n        Polish\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_American" title="Belgian American">\n        Belgian\n       </a>\n       ancestry. People of\n       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Americans" title="Scandinavian Americans">\n        Scandinavian\n       </a>\n       descent, and those of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finnish_American" title="Finnish American">\n        Finnish\n       </a>\n       ancestry, have a notable presence in the Upper Peninsula. Western Michigan is known for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_American" title="Dutch American">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       heritage of many residents (the highest concentration of any state), especially in\n       <a href="/wiki/Holland,_Michigan" title="Holland, Michigan">\n        Holland\n       </a>\n       and metropolitan Grand Rapids.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       African-Americans, who came to Detroit and other northern cities in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">\n        Great Migration\n       </a>\n       of the early 20th century, form a majority of the population of the city of Detroit and of other cities, including Flint and\n       <a href="/wiki/Benton_Harbor,_Michigan" title="Benton Harbor, Michigan">\n        Benton Harbor\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2007 about 300,000 people in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_Michigan" title="Southeastern Michigan">\n        Southeastern Michigan\n       </a>\n       trace their descent from the Middle East.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">\n        Dearborn\n       </a>\n       has a sizeable\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_American" title="Arab American">\n        Arab\n       </a>\n       community, with many\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian/Chaldean/Syriac_Americans" title="Assyrian/Chaldean/Syriac Americans">\n        Assyrian/Chaldean/Syriac\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_American" title="Lebanese American">\n        Lebanese\n       </a>\n       who immigrated for jobs in the auto industry in the 1920s along with more recent\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yemeni_American" title="Yemeni American">\n        Yemenis\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Americans" title="Iraqi Americans">\n        Iraqis\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2007, almost 8,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">\n        Hmong people\n       </a>\n       lived in the State of Michigan, about double their 1999 presence in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaiser2_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kaiser2-68">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2007 most lived in northeastern Detroit, but they had been increasingly moving to Pontiac and Warren.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michdaily_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Michdaily-69">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 2015 the number of Hmong in the Detroit city limits had significantly declined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosenremaining_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rosenremaining-70">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       hosts a statewide Hmong New Year Festival.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michdaily_69-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Michdaily-69">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Hmong community also had a prominent portrayal in the 2008 film\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Gran_Torino" title="Gran Torino">\n         Gran Torino\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which was set in\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">\n        Detroit\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2015, 80% of Michigan\'s Japanese population lived in the counties of Macomb, Oakland, Washtenaw, and Wayne in the Detroit and Ann Arbor areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilkinsonSookp158_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WilkinsonSookp158-71">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of April 2013, the largest Japanese national population is in\n       <a href="/wiki/Novi,_Michigan" title="Novi, Michigan">\n        Novi\n       </a>\n       , with 2,666 Japanese residents, and the next largest populations are respectively in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor,_Michigan" title="Ann Arbor, Michigan">\n        Ann Arbor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Bloomfield_Township,_Michigan" title="West Bloomfield Township, Michigan">\n        West Bloomfield Township\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Farmington_Hills,_Michigan" title="Farmington Hills, Michigan">\n        Farmington Hills\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_Creek,_Michigan" title="Battle Creek, Michigan">\n        Battle Creek\n       </a>\n       . The state has 481 Japanese employment facilities providing 35,554 local jobs. 391 of them are in Southeast Michigan, providing 20,816 jobs, and the 90 in other regions in the state provide 14,738 jobs. The Japanese Direct Investment Survey of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Consulate-General_of_Japan,_Detroit" title="Consulate-General of Japan, Detroit">\n        Consulate-General of Japan, Detroit\n       </a>\n       stated that over 2,208 additional Japanese residents were employed in the State of Michigan as of October 1, 2012, than in 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the 1990s the Japanese population of Michigan experienced an increase, and many Japanese people with children moved to particular areas for their proximity to Japanese grocery stores and high-performing schools.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilkinsonSookp158_71-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WilkinsonSookp158-71">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A person from Michigan is called a\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigander" title="Michigander">\n        Michigander\n       </a>\n       or Michiganian;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       also at times, but rarely, a "Michiganite".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Residents of the Upper Peninsula are sometimes referred to as "Yoopers" (a phonetic pronunciation of "U.P.ers"), and Upper Peninsula residents sometimes refer to those from the Lower Peninsula as "trolls" because they live below the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Bridge" title="Mackinac Bridge">\n        bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_data">\n        Birth data\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of 2011, 34.3% of Michigan\'s children under the age of one belonged to racial or ethnic minority groups, meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Note: Percentages in the table can exceed 100% as Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race.\n       </i>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <caption>\n        Live Births by Race/Ethnicity of   <td>\n         <b>\n          113,312\n         </b>\n         (100%)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">\n        Languages\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">\n          Vietnamese\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">\n          Japanese\n         </a>\n         , and\n         <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">\n          Korean\n         </a>\n         (tied)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.16%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       As of 2010, 91.11% (8,507,947) of Michigan residents age five and older spoke only\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       at home, while 2.93% (273,981) spoke\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       , 1.04% (97,559)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       , 0.44% (41,189)\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       , 0.36% (33,648)\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       (which includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">\n        Mandarin\n       </a>\n       ), 0.31% (28,891)\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       , 0.29% (27,019)\n       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">\n        Polish\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people#Language" title="Assyrian people">\n        Syriac languages\n       </a>\n       (such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Aramaic_languages" title="Neo-Aramaic languages">\n        Modern Aramaic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Neo-Aramaic" title="Northeastern Neo-Aramaic">\n        Northeastern Neo-Aramaic\n       </a>\n       ) was spoken as a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_language" title="Main language">\n        main language\n       </a>\n       by 0.25% (23,420) of the population over the age of five. In total, 8.89% (830,281) of Michigan\'s population age 5 and older spoke a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">\n        mother language\n       </a>\n       other than English.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data-80">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n  <div style="width:1px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:mediumblue">\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:left; text-indent:15px;">\n 0.5\n         </span>\n         <div style="width:1px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:mediumblue">\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a     Hinduism\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         <b>\n          0.5\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <span style="display:none;">\n          0.5\n         </span>\n         <div style="width:1px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:mediumblue">\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Other Faiths\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         <b>\n          1.5\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <span style="display:none;">\n          1.5\n <tr>\n        <td>\n         Don\'t Know / No Answer\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         <b>\n          1\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <span style="display:none;">\n          1\n         </span>\n         <div style="width:2px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkorange">\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Total\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          100\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <span style="display:none;">\n          100\n         </span>\n         <div style="width:200px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:grey">\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The Roman Catholic Church has six dioceses and one archdiocese in Michigan;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Gaylord" title="Diocese of Gaylord">\n        Gaylord\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Grand_Rapids" title="Diocese of Grand Rapids">\n        Grand Rapids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Kalamazoo" title="Diocese of Kalamazoo">\n        Kalamazoo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Lansing" title="Diocese of Lansing">\n        Lansing\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Marquette" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Marquette">\n        Marquette\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Saginaw" title="Diocese of Saginaw">\n        Saginaw\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Detroit" title="Archdiocese of Detroit">\n        Detroit\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Roman Catholic Church is the largest denomination by number of adherents, according to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">\n        Association of Religion Data Archives\n       </a>\n       (ARDA) 2010 survey, with 1,717,296 adherents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-83">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Roman Catholic Church was the only organized religion in Michigan until the 19th century, reflecting the territory\'s French colonial roots. Detroit\'s Saint Anne\'s parish, established in 1701 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Antoine_de_la_Mothe_Cadillac" title="Antoine de la Mothe Cadillac">\n        Antoine de la Mothe Cadillac\n       </a>\n       , is the second-oldest Roman Catholic parish in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On March 8, 1833, the Holy See formally established a diocese in the Michigan territory, which included all of Michigan, Wisconsin, Minnesota, and the Dakotas east of the Mississippi River. When Michigan became a state in 1837, the boundary of the Diocese of Detroit was redrawn to coincide with that of the State; the other dioceses were later carved out from the Diocese of Detroit but remain part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_Province" title="Ecclesiastical Province">\n        Ecclesiastical Province\n       </a>\n       of Detroit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2010, the largest Protestant denominations were the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">\n        United Methodist Church\n       </a>\n       with 228,521 adherents; followed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church%E2%80%93Missouri_Synod" title="Lutheran Church\xe2\x80\x93Missouri Synod">\n        Lutheran Church\xe2\x80\x93Missouri Synod\n       </a>\n       with 219,618; and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">\n        Evangelical Lutheran Church in America\n       </a>\n       with 120,598 adherents. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Christian_Reformed_Church_in_North_America" title="Christian Reformed Church in North America">\n        Christian Reformed Church in North America\n       </a>\n       had almost 100,000 members and over 230 congregations in Michigan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Church_in_America" title="Reformed Church in America">\n        Reformed Church in America\n       </a>\n       had 76,000 members and 154 congregations in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the same survey, Jewish adherents in the state of Michigan were estimated at 44,382, and Muslims at 120,351.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church" title="Lutheran Church">\n        Lutheran Church\n       </a>\n       was introduced by\n       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">\n        German\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">\n        Scandinavian\n       </a>\n       immigrants; Lutheranism is the second largest religious denomination in the state. The first Jewish synagogue in the state was\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temple_Beth_El_(Detroit,_Michigan)" title="Temple Beth El (Detroit, Michigan)">\n        Temple Beth El\n       </a>\n       , founded by twelve German Jewish families in Detroit in 1850.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In West Michigan, Dutch immigrants fled from the specter of religious persecution and famine in the Netherlands around 1850 and settled in and around what is now Holland, Michigan, establishing a "colony" on American soil that fervently held onto Calvinist doctrine that established a significant presence of Reformed churches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Islam was introduced by immigrants from the Near East during the 20th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan is home to the largest mosque in North America, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Center_of_America" title="Islamic Center of America">\n        Islamic Center of America\n       </a>\n       in Dearborn.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_Creek" title="Battle Creek">\n        Battle Creek\n       </a>\n       , Michigan is also the birthplace of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">\n        Seventh-day Adventist Church\n       </a>\n       , which was founded on May 21, 1863.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adventist_org_92-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Adventist_org-92">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_indian_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-New_indian-93">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Michigan" title="List of companies based in Michigan">\n        List of companies based in Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_metropolitan_Detroit" title="Economy of metropolitan Detroit">\n        Economy of metropolitan Detroit\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Michigan locations by per capita income">\n        Michigan locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg/220px-2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg"
