//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg/440px-2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2007_Ford_Shelby_GT500_Detroit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Michigan is the center of the American automotive industry. Pictured is the\n         <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Mustang" title="Shelby Mustang">\n          Ford Shelby GT500\n         </a>\n         at the\n         <a href="/wiki/North_American_International_Auto_Show" title="North American International Auto Show">\n          North American International Auto Show\n         </a>\n         in Detroit. The GT500 is manufactured in Ford\'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Flat_Rock,_Michigan" title="Flat Rock, Michigan">\n          Flat Rock, Michigan\n         </a>\n         , assembly plant.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. Economic Development Administration estimated Michigan\'s 2014 gross state product to be $417.306 billion, ranking 13th out of the 50 states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Labor_Statistics" title="Bureau of Labor Statistics">\n        Bureau of Labor Statistics\n       </a>\n       , as of October 2015, the state\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of U.S. states by unemployment rate">\n        seasonally adjusted unemployment rate\n       </a>\n       is estimated at 5.0%.\n 26\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wolverine_World_Wide" title="Wolverine World Wide">\n          Wolverine World Wide\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         806\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         27\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metaldyne" title="Metaldyne">\n          Metaldyne Performance\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         812\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         28\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Universal_Forest_Products" title="Universal Forest Products">\n          Universal Forest\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         821\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         29\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Diplomat Pharmacy\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         946\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         30\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tower_International" title="Tower International">\n          Tower International\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         956\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="5">\n         <i>\n          Further information:\n         </i>\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_companies" title="List of Michigan companies">\n          List of Michigan companies\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         <p>\n          <i>\n           <b>\n            Source\n           </b>\n          </i>\n          :\n          <i>\n           Fortune\n          </i>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fortune_Michigan_97-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-Fortune_Michigan-97">\n            [94]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </p>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Products and services include automobiles, food products, information technology, aerospace, military equipment, furniture, and mining of copper and iron ore. Michigan is the third leading grower of\n       <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">\n        Christmas trees\n       </a>\n       with 60,520 acres (245\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of land dedicated to Christmas tree farming.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The beverage\n       <a href="/wiki/Vernors" title="Vernors">\n        Vernors\n       </a>\n       was invented in Michigan in 1866, sharing the title of oldest soft drink with\n       <a href="/wiki/Hires_Root_Beer" title="Hires Root Beer">\n        Hires Root Beer\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Faygo" title="Faygo">\n        Faygo\n       </a>\n       was founded in Detroit on November 4, 1907. Two of the top four pizza chains were founded in Michigan and are headquartered there:\n       <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino\'s Pizza">\n        Domino\'s Pizza\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Monaghan" title="Tom Monaghan">\n        Tom Monaghan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Little_Caesars" title="Little Caesars">\n        Little Caesars\n       </a>\n       Pizza by\n       <a href="/wiki/Mike_Ilitch" title="Mike Ilitch">\n        Mike Ilitch\n       </a>\n       . Michigan became the 24th\n       <a href="/wiki/Right-to-work_law" title="Right-to-work law">\n        Right to Work\n       </a>\n       state in U.S. in 2012.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since 2009, GM, Ford and Chrysler have managed a significant reorganization of their benefit funds structure after a volatile stock market which followed the\n       <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">\n        September 11 attacks\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Early_2000s_recession" title="Early 2000s recession">\n        early 2000s recession\n       </a>\n       impacted their respective U.S. pension and benefit funds (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OPEB" title="OPEB">\n        OPEB\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       General Motors, Ford, and Chrysler reached agreements with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">\n        United Auto Workers\n       </a>\n       Union to transfer the liabilities for their respective health care and benefit funds to a 501(c)(9)\n       <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_Employee_Beneficiary_Association" title="Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association">\n        Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association\n       </a>\n       (VEBA). Manufacturing in the state grew 6.6% from 2001 to 2006,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-102">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the high speculative price of oil became a factor for the U.S. auto industry during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" title="Late-2000s recession">\n        economic crisis of 2008\n       </a>\n       impacting industry revenues. In 2009, GM and Chrysler emerged from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chapter_11" title="Chapter 11">\n        Chapter 11\n       </a>\n       restructurings with financing provided in part by the U.S. and Canadian governments.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garrett_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Garrett-103">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stoll_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Stoll-104">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       GM began its\n       <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">\n        initial public offering\n       </a>\n       (IPO) of stock in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPO_105-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IPO-105">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For 2010, the Big Three domestic automakers have reported significant profits indicating the beginning of rebound.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schroeder_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Schroeder-107">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cwiek_109-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cwiek-109">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2002\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Michigan&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Michigan ranked fourth in the U.S. in high tech employment with 568,000 high tech workers, which includes 70,000 in the automotive industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MEDCHiTech_110-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MEDCHiTech-110">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan typically ranks third or fourth in overall\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_%26_development" title="Research &amp; development">\n        Research &amp; development\n       </a>\n       (R&amp;D) expenditures in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MEDC1_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MEDC1-30">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSF_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSF-31">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its research and development, which includes automotive, comprises a higher percentage of the state\'s overall gross domestic product than for any other U.S. state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state is an important source of engineering job opportunities. The domestic auto industry accounts directly and indirectly for one of every ten jobs in the U.S.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan was second in the U.S. in 2004 for new corporate facilities and expansions. From 1997 to 2004, Michigan was the only state to top the 10,000 mark for the number of major new developments;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAM_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAM-28">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       however, the effects of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_2000s_recession" title="Late 2000s recession">\n        late 2000s recession\n       </a>\n       have slowed the state\'s economy. In 2008, Michigan placed third in a site selection survey among the states for luring new business which measured capital investment and new job creation per one million population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-siteselection_114-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-siteselection-114">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In August 2009, Michigan and Detroit\'s auto industry received $1.36 B in grants from the U.S. Department of Energy for the manufacture of electric vehicle technologies which is expected to generate 6,800 immediate jobs and employ 40,000 in the state by 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-priddle_115-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-priddle-115">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       From 2007 to 2009, Michigan ranked 3rd in the U.S. for new corporate facilities and expansions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lane_116-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lane-116">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Medernach_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Medernach-117">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As leading research institutions, the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">\n        Michigan State University\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University" title="Wayne State University">\n        Wayne State University\n       </a>\n       are important partners in the state\'s economy and its\n       <a href="/wiki/University_Research_Corridor" title="University Research Corridor">\n        University Research Corridor\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_Research_Corridor_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-University_Research_Corridor-32">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s public universities attract more than $1.5 B in research and development grants each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bruns_33-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bruns-33">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Superconducting_Cyclotron_Laboratory" title="National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory">\n        National Superconducting Cyclotron Laboratory\n       </a>\n       is located at Michigan State University. Michigan\'s workforce is well-educated and highly skilled, making it attractive to companies. It has the third highest number of engineering graduates nationally.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Detroit Metropolitan Airport">\n        Detroit Metropolitan Airport\n       </a>\n       is one of the nation\'s most recently expanded and modernized airports with six major runways, and large aircraft maintenance facilities capable of servicing and repairing a\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">\n        Boeing 747\n       </a>\n       and is a major hub for\n       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">\n        Delta Air Lines\n       </a>\n       . Michigan\'s schools and colleges rank among the nation\'s best. The state has maintained its early commitment to public education. The state\'s infrastructure gives it a competitive edge; Michigan has 38\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep-water_port" title="Deep-water port">\n        deep water ports\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2007, Bank of America announced that it would commit $25\xc2\xa0billion to community development in Michigan following its acquisition of LaSalle Bank in\n       <a href="/wiki/Troy,_Michigan" title="Troy, Michigan">\n        Troy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bank_120-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bank-120">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan led the nation in job creation improvement in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png">\n         <img alt="A treemap depicting the distribution of Michigan\'s jobs as percentages of entire workforce" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="2278" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png/220px-Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png/330px-Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png/440px-Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Occupations_by_Share_in_Michigan.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Distribution of Michigan\'s jobs as percentages of entire workforce.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">\n        Taxation\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s personal\n       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">\n        income tax\n       </a>\n       is set to a flat rate of 4.25%. In addition, 22\xc2\xa0cities impose income taxes; rates are set at 1% for residents and 0.5% for non-residents in all but four cities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-income-tax_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-city-income-tax-122">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s state\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       is 6%, though items such as food and medication are exempted from sales tax.\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        Property taxes\n       </a>\n       are assessed on the local level, but every property owner\'s local assessment contributes six\n       <a href="/wiki/Mill_(currency)" title="Mill (currency)">\n        mills\n       </a>\n       (a rate of $6 per $1000 of property value) to the statutory State Education Tax. Property taxes are appealable to local boards of review and need the approval of the local electorate to exceed millage rates prescribed by state law and local charters. In 2011, the state repealed its business tax and replaced it with a 6% corporate income tax which substantially reduced taxes on business.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Article IX of the Constitution of the State of Michigan also provides limitations on how much the state can tax.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state also levies a 6%\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       within the state and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Use_tax" title="Use tax">\n        Use tax\n       </a>\n       on goods purchased outside the state (that are brought in and used in state).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The use tax applies to internet sales/purchases from outside Michigan, and is equivalent to the sales tax.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">\n        Agriculture\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_Cherries,_2009_July.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="640" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg/220px-Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg/330px-Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg/440px-Michigan_Cherries%2C_2009_July.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_Cherries,_2009_July.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Michigan is the leading U.S. producer of\n         <a href="/wiki/Prunus_cerasus" title="Prunus cerasus">\n          tart cherries\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Blueberry" title="Blueberry">\n          blueberries\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pickling_cucumber" title="Pickling cucumber">\n          pickling cucumbers\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Navy_bean" title="Navy bean">\n          navy beans\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Petunia" title="Petunia">\n          petunias\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_production_in_Michigan" title="Cherry production in Michigan">\n        Cherry production in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A wide variety of commodity crops, fruits, and vegetables are grown in Michigan, making it second only to California among U.S. states in the diversity of its agriculture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state has 54,800 farms utilizing 10,000,000 acres (40,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of land which sold $6.49\xc2\xa0billion worth of products in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The most valuable agricultural product is milk. Leading crops include corn, soybeans, flowers, wheat, sugar beets and potatoes. Livestock in the state included 1 million cattle, 1\xc2\xa0million hogs, 78,000 sheep and over 3\xc2\xa0million chickens. Livestock products accounted for 38% of the value of agricultural products while crops accounted for the majority.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is a leading grower of fruit in the U.S., including blueberries,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_production_in_Michigan" title="Cherry production in Michigan">\n        tart cherries\n       </a>\n       , apples, grapes, and peaches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MIAG_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MIAG-34">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Plums, pears, and strawberries are also grown. These fruits are mainly grown in\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Michigan" title="West Michigan">\n        West Michigan\n       </a>\n       due to the moderating effect of Lake Michigan on the climate. There is also significant fruit production, especially cherries, but also grapes, apples, and other fruits, in Northwest Michigan along Lake Michigan. Michigan produces\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_wine" title="Michigan wine">\n        wines\n       </a>\n       , beers and a multitude of processed food products.\n       <a href="/wiki/Kellogg%27s" title="Kellogg\'s">\n        Kellogg\'s\n       </a>\n       cereal is based in Battle Creek, Michigan and processes many locally grown foods. Thornapple Valley,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ball_Park_Franks" title="Ball Park Franks">\n        Ball Park Franks\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Koegel_Meat_Company" title="Koegel Meat Company">\n        Koegel Meat Company\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_National" title="Hebrew National">\n        Hebrew National\n       </a>\n       sausage companies are all based in Michigan.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is home to very fertile land in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tri-Cities_(Michigan)" title="Tri-Cities (Michigan)">\n        Saginaw Valley\n       </a>\n       and "\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Thumb" title="The Thumb">\n        Thumb\n       </a>\n       " areas. Products grown there include corn, sugar beets, navy beans, and soy beans. Sugar beet harvesting usually begins the first of October. It takes the sugar factories about five months to process the 3.7\xc2\xa0million tons of sugarbeets into 485,000 tons of pure, white sugar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s largest sugar refiner,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_Sugar_Company" title="Michigan Sugar Company">\n        Michigan Sugar Company\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is the largest east of the Mississippi River and the fourth largest in the nation. Michigan Sugar brand names are Pioneer Sugar and the newly incorporated Big Chief Sugar. Potatoes are grown in\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan" title="Northern Michigan">\n        Northern Michigan\n       </a>\n       , and corn is dominant in\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Michigan" title="Central Michigan">\n        Central Michigan\n       </a>\n       . Alfalfa, cucumbers, and asparagus are also grown.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Landmarks_in_Michigan" title="List of National Historic Landmarks in Michigan">\n        List of National Historic Landmarks in Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Registered_Historic_Places_in_Michigan" title="List of Registered Historic Places in Michigan">\n        List of Registered Historic Places in Michigan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Michigan" title="List of museums in Michigan">\n        List of museums in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s tourists spend $17.2\xc2\xa0billion per year in the state, supporting 193,000 tourism jobs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan\'s tourism website ranks among the busiest in the nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Destinations draw vacationers, hunters, and nature enthusiasts from across the United States and Canada. Michigan is fifty percent forest land, much of it quite remote. The forests, lakes and thousands of miles of beaches are top attractions. Event tourism draws large numbers to occasions like the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tulip_Time_Festival" title="Tulip Time Festival">\n        Tulip Time Festival\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Cherry_Festival" title="National Cherry Festival">\n        National Cherry Festival\n       </a>\n       . In 2006, the Michigan State Board of Education mandated that all public schools in the state hold their first day of school after the Labor Day holiday, in accordance with the new Post Labor Day School law. A survey found that 70% of all tourism business comes directly from Michigan residents, and the Michigan Hotel, Motel, &amp; Resort Association claimed that the shorter summer in between school years cut into the annual tourism season in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_metropolitan_Detroit" title="Tourism in metropolitan Detroit">\n        Tourism in metropolitan Detroit\n       </a>\n       draws visitors to leading attractions, especially\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Henry_Ford" title="The Henry Ford">\n        The Henry Ford\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Institute_of_Arts" title="Detroit Institute of Arts">\n        Detroit Institute of Arts\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Zoo" title="Detroit Zoo">\n        Detroit Zoo\n       </a>\n       , and to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Detroit" title="Sports in Detroit">\n        sports in Detroit\n       </a>\n       . Other museums include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Historical_Museum" title="Detroit Historical Museum">\n        Detroit Historical Museum\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_H._Wright_Museum_of_African_American_History" title="Charles H. Wright Museum of African American History">\n        Charles H. Wright Museum of African American History\n       </a>\n       , museums in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cranbrook_Educational_Community" title="Cranbrook Educational Community">\n        Cranbrook Educational Community\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arab_American_National_Museum" title="Arab American National Museum">\n        Arab American National Museum\n       </a>\n       . The metro area offers four major casinos,\n       <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Detroit" title="MGM Grand Detroit">\n        MGM Grand Detroit\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greektown_Casino" title="Greektown Casino">\n        Greektown\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_City_Casino" title="Motor City Casino">\n        Motor City\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Windsor" title="Caesars Windsor">\n        Caesars Windsor\n       </a>\n       in Windsor, Ontario, Canada; moreover, Detroit is the largest American city and metropolitan region to offer casino resorts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mink_135-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mink-135">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holland_State_Park.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1720" data-file-width="2579" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Holland_State_Park.jpg/220px-Holland_State_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Holland_State_Park.jpg/330px-Holland_State_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Holland_State_Park.jpg/440px-Holland_State_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holland_State_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lake Michigan beach at\n         <a href="/wiki/Holland_State_Park" title="Holland State Park">\n          Holland State Park\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Hunting and fishing are significant industries in the state. Charter boats are based in many Great Lakes cities to fish for salmon, trout, walleye and perch. Michigan ranks first in the nation in licensed hunters (over one million) who contribute $2\xc2\xa0billion annually to its economy. Over three-quarters of a million hunters participate in\n       <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">\n        white-tailed deer\n       </a>\n       season alone. Many school districts in rural areas of Michigan cancel school on the opening day of firearm deer season, because of attendance concerns.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s Department of Natural Resources manages the largest dedicated state forest system in the nation. The forest products industry and recreational users contribute $12\xc2\xa0billion and 200,000 associated jobs annually to the state\'s economy. Public hiking and hunting access has also been secured in extensive commercial forests. The state has the highest number of golf courses and registered\n       <a href="/wiki/Snowmobile" title="Snowmobile">\n        snowmobiles\n       </a>\n       in the nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state has numerous\n       <a href="/wiki/Historical_marker" title="Historical marker">\n        historical markers\n       </a>\n       , which can themselves become the center of a tour.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Circle_Tour" title="Great Lakes Circle Tour">\n        Great Lakes Circle Tour\n       </a>\n       is a designated scenic road system connecting all of the Great Lakes and the St. Lawrence River.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With its position in relation to the Great Lakes and the countless ships that have foundered over the many years in which they have been used as a transport route for people and bulk cargo, Michigan is a world-class scuba diving destination. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Underwater_Preserves" title="Michigan Underwater Preserves">\n        Michigan Underwater Preserves\n       </a>\n       are 11 underwater areas where wrecks are protected for the benefit of sport divers.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_international_crossings">\n        Canadian international crossings\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG/220px-Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG/330px-Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG/440px-Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michigan_entrance_sign.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Welcome sign\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan has nine international road crossings with\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       , Canada:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ambassador_Bridge" title="Ambassador Bridge">\n         Ambassador Bridge\n        </a>\n        , North America\'s busiest international border, crossing the\n        <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">\n         Detroit River\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Blue_Water_Bridge" title="Blue Water Bridge">\n         Blue Water Bridge\n        </a>\n        , a twin-span bridge (\n        <a href="/wiki/Port_Huron,_Michigan" title="Port Huron, Michigan">\n         Port Huron, Michigan\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Point_Edward,_Ontario" title="Point Edward, Ontario">\n         Point Edward, Ontario\n        </a>\n        , but the larger city of\n        <a href="/wiki/Sarnia" title="Sarnia">\n         Sarnia\n        </a>\n        is usually referred to on the Canadian side)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Blue Water Ferry (\n        <a href="/wiki/Marine_City,_Michigan" title="Marine City, Michigan">\n         Marine City, Michigan\n        </a>\n        , and Sombra, Ontario)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Central_Railway_Tunnel" title="Michigan Central Railway Tunnel">\n         Canadian Pacific Railway tunnel\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Detroit%E2%80%93Windsor_Truck_Ferry" title="Detroit\xe2\x80\x93Windsor Truck Ferry">\n         Detroit\xe2\x80\x93Windsor Truck Ferry\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">\n         Detroit\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">\n         Windsor\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Detroit%E2%80%93Windsor_Tunnel" title="Detroit\xe2\x80\x93Windsor Tunnel">\n         Detroit\xe2\x80\x93Windsor Tunnel\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie_International_Bridge" title="Sault Ste. Marie International Bridge">\n         International Bridge\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Michigan" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan">\n         Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Ontario" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Ontario">\n         Sault Ste. Marie, Ontario\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/St._Clair_Tunnel" title="St. Clair Tunnel">\n         St. Clair River Railway Tunnel\n        </a>\n        (Port Huron and Sarnia)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walpole_Island" title="Walpole Island">\n         Walpole Island\n        </a>\n        Ferry (\n        <a href="/wiki/Algonac,_Michigan" title="Algonac, Michigan">\n         Algonac, Michigan\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walpole_Island" title="Walpole Island">\n         Walpole Island\n        </a>\n        First Nation, Ontario)\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       A second international bridge is currently under consideration between Detroit and Windsor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Railroads">\n        Railroads\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_railroads" title="List of Michigan railroads">\n        List of Michigan railroads\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_railroads_in_Michigan" title="History of railroads in Michigan">\n        History of railroads in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is served by four\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">\n        Class I railroads\n       </a>\n       : the\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Railway" title="Canadian National Railway">\n        Canadian National Railway\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">\n        Canadian Pacific Railway\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">\n        CSX Transportation\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">\n        Norfolk Southern Railway\n       </a>\n       . These are augmented by several dozen\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short_line_railroad" title="Short line railroad">\n        short line railroads\n       </a>\n       . The vast majority of rail service in Michigan is devoted to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freight_rail" title="Freight rail">\n        freight\n       </a>\n       , with Amtrak and various scenic railroads the exceptions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Services" title="Michigan Services">\n        Michigan Services\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       passenger rail services the state, connecting many southern and western Michigan cities to Chicago, Illinois. There are plans for\n       <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">\n        commuter rail\n       </a>\n       for Detroit and its suburbs (see\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SEMCOG_Commuter_Rail" title="SEMCOG Commuter Rail">\n        SEMCOG Commuter Rail\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">\n        <a href="#cite_note-141">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways">\n        Roadways\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="953" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg/220px-Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg/330px-Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg/440px-Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mackinac_Bridge_Sunset.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Bridge" title="Mackinac Bridge">\n          Mackinac Bridge\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Trunkline_Highway_System" title="Michigan State Trunkline Highway System">\n        Michigan State Trunkline Highway System\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_County-Designated_Highways_in_Michigan" title="List of County-Designated Highways in Michigan">\n        County-Designated Highways in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Michigan" title="Interstate 75 in Michigan">\n         Interstate\xc2\xa075\n        </a>\n        (I-75) is the main thoroughfare between Detroit,\n        <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">\n         Flint\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Saginaw,_Michigan" title="Saginaw, Michigan">\n         Saginaw\n        </a>\n        extending north to\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Michigan" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan">\n         Sault Ste. Marie\n        </a>\n        and providing access to\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Ontario" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Ontario">\n         Sault Ste. Marie, Ontario\n        </a>\n        . The freeway crosses the\n        <a href="/wiki/Mackinac_Bridge" title="Mackinac Bridge">\n         Mackinac Bridge\n        </a>\n        between the Lower and Upper Peninsulas. Auxiliary highways include\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_275_(Michigan)" title="Interstate 275 (Michigan)">\n         I-275\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_375_(Michigan)" title="Interstate 375 (Michigan)">\n         I-375\n        </a>\n        in Detroit;\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_475_(Michigan)" title="Interstate 475 (Michigan)">\n         I-475\n        </a>\n        in Flint; and\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_675_(Michigan)" title="Interstate 675 (Michigan)">\n         I-675\n        </a>\n        in Saginaw.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_69_in_Michigan" title="Interstate 69 in Michigan">\n         I-69\n        </a>\n        enters the state near the Michigan\xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n         Ohio\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">\n         Indiana\n        </a>\n        border, and it extends to\n        <a href="/wiki/Port_Huron,_Michigan" title="Port Huron, Michigan">\n         Port Huron\n        </a>\n        and provides access to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Blue_Water_Bridge" title="Blue Water Bridge">\n         Blue Water Bridge\n        </a>\n        crossing into\n        <a href="/wiki/Sarnia" title="Sarnia">\n         Sarnia\n        </a>\n        , Ontario.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_94_in_Michigan" title="Interstate 94 in Michigan">\n         I-94\n        </a>\n        enters the western end of the state at the Indiana border, and it travels east to Detroit and then northeast to Port Huron and ties in with I-69.\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_194_(Michigan)" title="Interstate 194 (Michigan)">\n         I-194\n        </a>\n        branches off from this freeway in\n        <a href="/wiki/Battle_Creek,_Michigan" title="Battle Creek, Michigan">\n         Battle Creek\n        </a>\n        . I-94 is the main artery between Chicago and Detroit.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_96" title="Interstate 96">\n         I-96\n        </a>\n        runs east\xe2\x80\x93west between Detroit and\n        <a href="/wiki/Muskegon,_Michigan" title="Muskegon, Michigan">\n         Muskegon\n        </a>\n        .\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_496" title="Interstate 496">\n         I-496\n        </a>\n        loops through\n        <a href="/wiki/Lansing,_Michigan" title="Lansing, Michigan">\n         Lansing\n        </a>\n        .\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_196" title="Interstate 196">\n         I-196\n        </a>\n        branches off from this freeway at\n        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Michigan" title="Grand Rapids, Michigan">\n         Grand Rapids\n        </a>\n        and connects to I-94 near\n        <a href="/wiki/Benton_Harbor,_Michigan" title="Benton Harbor, Michigan">\n         Benton Harbor\n        </a>\n        .\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_696" title="Interstate 696">\n         I-696\n        </a>\n        branches off from this freeway at\n        <a href="/wiki/Novi,_Michigan" title="Novi, Michigan">\n         Novi\n        </a>\n        and connects to I-94 near\n        <a href="/wiki/St._Clair_Shores,_Michigan" title="St. Clair Shores, Michigan">\n         St Clair Shores\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_2_in_Michigan" title="U.S. Route 2 in Michigan">\n         US Highway\xc2\xa02\n        </a>\n        (US\xc2\xa02) enters Michigan at the city of\n        <a href="/wiki/Ironwood,_Michigan" title="Ironwood, Michigan">\n         Ironwood\n        </a>\n        and travels east to the town of\n        <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Falls,_Michigan" title="Crystal Falls, Michigan">\n         Crystal Falls\n        </a>\n        , where it turns south and briefly re-enters\n        <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">\n         Wisconsin\n        </a>\n        northwest of\n        <a href="/wiki/Florence_(CDP),_Wisconsin" title="Florence (CDP), Wisconsin">\n         Florence\n        </a>\n        . It re-enters Michigan north of\n        <a href="/wiki/Iron_Mountain,_Michigan" title="Iron Mountain, Michigan">\n         Iron Mountain\n        </a>\n        and continues through the Upper Peninsula of Michigan to the cities of\n        <a href="/wiki/Escanaba,_Michigan" title="Escanaba, Michigan">\n         Escanaba\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Manistique,_Michigan" title="Manistique, Michigan">\n         Manistique\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/St._Ignace,_Michigan" title="St. Ignace, Michigan">\n         St. Ignace\n        </a>\n        . Along the way, it cuts through the\n        <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_National_Forest" title="Ottawa National Forest">\n         Ottawa\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Hiawatha_National_Forest" title="Hiawatha National Forest">\n         Hiawatha\n        </a>\n        national forests and follows the northern shore of\n        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">\n         Lake Michigan\n        </a>\n        . Its eastern terminus lies at exit\xc2\xa0344 on I-75, just north of the Mackinac Bridge.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">\n        Airports\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Michigan" title="List of airports in Michigan">\n        List of airports in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detroit_Metropolitan_Wayne_County_Airport" title="Detroit Metropolitan Wayne County Airport">\n        Detroit Metropolitan Wayne County Airport\n       </a>\n       , located in the western suburb of\n       <a href="/wiki/Romulus,_Michigan" title="Romulus, Michigan">\n        Romulus\n       </a>\n       , was in 2010 the 16th busiest airfield in North America measured by passenger traffic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford_International_Airport" title="Gerald R. Ford International Airport">\n        Gerald R. Ford International Airport\n       </a>\n       in Grand Rapids is the next busiest airport in the state, served by eight airlines to 23 destinations. Flint\n       <a href="/wiki/Bishop_International_Airport" title="Bishop International Airport">\n        Bishop International Airport\n       </a>\n       is the third largest airport in the state, served by four airlines to several primary hubs. Smaller regional and local airports are located throughout the state including on several islands.\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Capital_Airport" title="Cherry Capital Airport">\n        Cherry Capital Airport\n       </a>\n       is located in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traverse_City" title="Traverse City">\n        Traverse City\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span id="Large_cities,_townships,_and_metropolitan_areas">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Large_cities.2C_townships.2C_and_metropolitan_areas">\n        Large cities, townships, and metropolitan areas\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DowntownDetroit.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/DowntownDetroit.jpg/220px-DowntownDetroit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/DowntownDetroit.jpg/330px-DowntownDetroit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/DowntownDetroit.jpg/440px-DowntownDetroit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DowntownDetroit.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Detroit skyline along the\n         <a href="/wiki/Detroit_International_Riverfront" title="Detroit International Riverfront">\n          International Riverfront\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grskyline2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="1024" height="57" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Grskyline2.jpg/220px-Grskyline2.jpg"
