391,569\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Other economically significant cities include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Battle_Creek,_Michigan" title="Battle Creek, Michigan">\n         Battle Creek\n        </a>\n        , known as "Cereal City", is the headquarters of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kellogg_Company" title="Kellogg Company">\n         Kellogg\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Benton_Harbor,_Michigan" title="Benton Harbor, Michigan">\n         Benton Harbor\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93\n        <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph,_Michigan" title="St. Joseph, Michigan">\n         St. Joseph\n        </a>\n        is the headquarters of\n        <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool_Corporation" title="Whirlpool Corporation">\n         Whirlpool Corporation\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/East_Lansing,_Michigan" title="East Lansing, Michigan">\n         East Lansing\n        </a>\n        is the home of\n        <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">\n         Michigan State University\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Holland,_Michigan" title="Holland, Michigan">\n         Holland\n        </a>\n        is the home of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tulip_Time" title="Tulip Time">\n         Tulip Time\n        </a>\n        , the largest tulip festival in the US.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jackson,_Michigan" title="Jackson, Michigan">\n         Jackson\n        </a>\n        is the headquarters of\n        <a href="/wiki/CMS_Energy" title="CMS Energy">\n         CMS Energy\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Manistee,_Michigan" title="Manistee, Michigan">\n         Manistee\n        </a>\n        is home to the world\'s largest salt plant, owned by\n        <a href="/wiki/Morton_Salt" title="Morton Salt">\n         Morton Salt\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Marquette,_Michigan" title="Marquette, Michigan">\n         Marquette\n        </a>\n        is the largest city in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Upper Peninsula of Michigan">\n         Upper Peninsula\n        </a>\n        with 19,661 people and home of\n        <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan_University" title="Northern Michigan University">\n         Northern Michigan University\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Midland,_Michigan" title="Midland, Michigan">\n         Midland\n        </a>\n        is the headquarters of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical_Company" title="Dow Chemical Company">\n         Dow Chemical Company\n        </a>\n        and the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dow_Corning_Corporation" title="Dow Corning Corporation">\n         Dow Corning Corporation\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Michigan" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan">\n         Sault Ste. Marie\n        </a>\n        is the home of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Soo_Locks" title="Soo Locks">\n         Soo Locks\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie_International_Bridge" title="Sault Ste. Marie International Bridge">\n         Sault Ste. Marie International Bridge\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Traverse_City,_Michigan" title="Traverse City, Michigan">\n         Traverse City\n        </a>\n        is the "Cherry Capital of the World", making Michigan the nation\'s largest producer of cherries and is also the largest city in\n        <a href="/wiki/Northern_Michigan" title="Northern Michigan">\n         Northern Michigan\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Half of the wealthiest communities in the state are located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_County,_Michigan" title="Oakland County, Michigan">\n        Oakland County\n       </a>\n       , just north of Detroit. Another wealthy community is located just east of the city, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Grosse_Pointe,_Michigan" title="Grosse Pointe, Michigan">\n        Grosse Pointe\n       </a>\n       . Only three of these cities are located outside of Metro Detroit. The city of Detroit itself, with a per capita income of $14,717, ranks 517th on the list of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michigan_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Michigan locations by per capita income">\n        Michigan locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Benton_Harbor,_Michigan" title="Benton Harbor, Michigan">\n        Benton Harbor\n       </a>\n       is the poorest city in Michigan, with a per capita income of $8,965, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Barton_Hills,_Michigan" title="Barton Hills, Michigan">\n        Barton Hills\n       </a>\n       is the richest with a per capita income of $110,683.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Michigan" title="List of colleges and universities in Michigan">\n        List of colleges and universities in Michigan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Michigan" title="List of high schools in Michigan">\n        List of high schools in Michigan\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s education system provides services to 1.6\xc2\xa0million K-12 students in public schools. More than 124,000 students attend private schools and an uncounted number are home-schooled under certain legal requirements.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The public school system has a $14.5\xc2\xa0billion budget in 2008\xe2\x80\x932009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n        <a href="#cite_note-148">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan has a number of public universities spread throughout the state and numerous private colleges as well. Michigan State University has the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_United_States_university_campuses_by_enrollment" title="List of largest United States university campuses by enrollment">\n        eighth largest\n       </a>\n       campus population of any U.S. school. Seven of the state\'s universities\xe2\x80\x94\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Michigan_University" title="Central Michigan University">\n        Central Michigan University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">\n        Michigan State University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Technological_University" title="Michigan Technological University">\n        Michigan Technological University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_University" title="Oakland University">\n        Oakland University\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_State_University" title="Wayne State University">\n        Wayne State University\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Michigan_University" title="Western Michigan University">\n        Western Michigan University\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94are classified as research universities by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching">\n        Carnegie Foundation\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n        <a href="#cite_note-149">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">\n        Culture\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">\n        Arts\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">\n        Music\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Michigan music is known for three music trends: early\n       <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">\n        punk rock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">\n        Motown\n       </a>\n       /soul music and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Techno_music" title="Techno music">\n        techno music\n       </a>\n       . Michigan musicians include\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Haley_%26_His_Comets" title="Bill Haley &amp; His Comets">\n        Bill Haley &amp; His Comets\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Supremes" title="The Supremes">\n        The Supremes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Marvelettes" title="The Marvelettes">\n        The Marvelettes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Temptations" title="The Temptations">\n        The Temptations\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Four_Tops" title="The Four Tops">\n        The Four Tops\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">\n        Stevie Wonder\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Gaye" title="Marvin Gaye">\n        Marvin Gaye\n       </a>\n       "The Prince of Soul",\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson_and_the_Miracles" title="Smokey Robinson and the Miracles">\n        Smokey Robinson and the Miracles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">\n        Aretha Franklin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mary_Wells" title="Mary Wells">\n        Mary Wells\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tommy_James_and_the_Shondells" title="Tommy James and the Shondells">\n        Tommy James and the Shondells\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/%3F_and_the_Mysterians" title="? and the Mysterians">\n        ? and the Mysterians\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Al_Green" title="Al Green">\n        Al Green\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Spinners_(American_R%26B_group)" title="The Spinners (American R&amp;B group)">\n        The Spinners\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Funk_Railroad" title="Grand Funk Railroad">\n        Grand Funk Railroad\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Knack" title="The Knack">\n        The Knack\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">\n        Madonna\n       </a>\n       "The Queen of Pop",\n       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Seger" title="Bob Seger">\n        Bob Seger\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ray_Parker_Jr." title="Ray Parker Jr.">\n        Ray Parker Jr.\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Aaliyah" title="Aaliyah">\n        Aaliyah\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">\n        Eminem\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kid_Rock" title="Kid Rock">\n        Kid Rock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jack_White" title="Jack White">\n        Jack White\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">\n        Big Sean\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper" title="Alice Cooper">\n        Alice Cooper\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_arts">\n        Performance arts\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Major theaters in Michigan include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fox_Theatre_(Detroit)" title="Fox Theatre (Detroit)">\n        Fox Theatre\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_Hall_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Music Hall Center for the Performing Arts">\n        Music Hall\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gem_Theatre" title="Gem Theatre">\n        Gem Theatre\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Masonic_Temple" title="Detroit Masonic Temple">\n        Masonic Temple Theatre\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Opera_House" title="Detroit Opera House">\n        Detroit Opera House\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fisher_Theatre" title="Fisher Theatre">\n        Fisher Theatre\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Fillmore_Detroit" title="The Fillmore Detroit">\n        The Fillmore Detroit\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew%27s_Hall" title="Saint Andrew\'s Hall">\n        Saint Andrew\'s Hall\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Majestic_Theater_(Detroit,_Michigan)" title="Majestic Theater (Detroit, Michigan)">\n        Majestic Theater\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Orchestra_Hall_(Detroit)" title="Orchestra Hall (Detroit)">\n        Orchestra Hall\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Nederlander_Organization" title="Nederlander Organization">\n        Nederlander Organization\n       </a>\n       , the largest controller of Broadway productions in New York City, originated in Detroit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Almanac2_150-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Almanac2-150">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Detroit Symphony Orchestra">\n        Detroit Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Motown_Motion_Picture_Studios" title="Motown Motion Picture Studios">\n        Motown Motion Picture Studios\n       </a>\n       with 535,000 square feet (49,700\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) produces movies in Detroit and the surrounding area based at the Pontiac Centerpoint Business Campus.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_professional_sports_teams" title="List of Michigan professional sports teams">\n        List of Michigan professional sports teams\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Michigan_sport_championships" title="List of Michigan sport championships">\n        List of Michigan sport championships\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan\'s major-league sports teams include:\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">\n        Detroit Tigers\n       </a>\n       baseball team,\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Lions" title="Detroit Lions">\n        Detroit Lions\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">\n        football\n       </a>\n       team,\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Red_Wings" title="Detroit Red Wings">\n        Detroit Red Wings\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">\n        ice hockey\n       </a>\n       team, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Pistons" title="Detroit Pistons">\n        Detroit Pistons\n       </a>\n       men\'s basketball team. All of Michigan\'s major league teams play in the Metro Detroit area.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Pistons played at Detroit\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cobo_Arena" title="Cobo Arena">\n        Cobo Arena\n       </a>\n       until 1978 and at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pontiac_Silverdome" title="Pontiac Silverdome">\n        Pontiac Silverdome\n       </a>\n       until 1988 when they moved into\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Palace_of_Auburn_Hills" title="The Palace of Auburn Hills">\n        The Palace of Auburn Hills\n       </a>\n       . The Detroit Lions played at\n       <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(Detroit)" title="Tiger Stadium (Detroit)">\n        Tiger Stadium\n       </a>\n       in Detroit until 1974, then moved to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pontiac_Silverdome" title="Pontiac Silverdome">\n        Pontiac Silverdome\n       </a>\n       where they played for 27 years between 1975 and 2002 before moving to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ford_Field" title="Ford Field">\n        Ford Field\n       </a>\n       in Detroit in 2002. The Detroit Tigers played at Tiger Stadium (formerly known as Navin Field and Briggs Stadium) from 1912 to 1999. In 2000 they moved to\n       <a href="/wiki/Comerica_Park" title="Comerica Park">\n        Comerica Park\n       </a>\n       . The Red Wings played at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympia_Stadium" title="Olympia Stadium">\n        Olympia Stadium\n       </a>\n       before moving to\n       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Louis_Arena" title="Joe Louis Arena">\n        Joe Louis Arena\n       </a>\n       in 1979. Professional hockey got its start in\n       <a href="/wiki/Houghton,_Michigan" title="Houghton, Michigan">\n        Houghton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       when the Portage Lakers were formed.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_International_Speedway" title="Michigan International Speedway">\n        Michigan International Speedway\n       </a>\n       is the site of\n       <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">\n        NASCAR\n       </a>\n       races and Detroit was formerly the site of a Formula One World Championship\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Grand_Prix" title="Detroit Grand Prix">\n        Grand Prix\n       </a>\n       race. From 1959 to 1961,\n       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Dragway" title="Detroit Dragway">\n        Detroit Dragway\n       </a>\n       hosted the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHRA" title="NHRA">\n        NHRA\n       </a>\n       \'s U.S. Nationals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Michigan is home to one of the major canoeing marathons: the 120-mile (190\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a href="/wiki/Au_Sable_River_Canoe_Marathon" title="Au Sable River Canoe Marathon">\n        Au Sable River Canoe Marathon\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Huron_to_Mackinac_Boat_Race" title="Port Huron to Mackinac Boat Race">\n        Port Huron to Mackinac Boat Race\n       </a>\n       is also a favorite.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Twenty-time Grand Slam champion\n       <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">\n        Serena Williams\n       </a>\n       was born in Saginaw. The\n       <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Artistic_Gymnastics_Championships" title="2011 World Artistic Gymnastics Championships">\n        2011 World Champion for Women\'s Artistic Gymnastics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jordyn_Wieber" title="Jordyn Wieber">\n        Jordyn Wieber\n       </a>\n       is from DeWitt. Wieber was also a member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_artistic_team_all-around" title="Gymnastics at the 2012 Summer Olympics \xe2\x80\x93 Women\'s artistic team all-around">\n        gold medal winning team\n       </a>\n       at the London Olympics in 2012.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Collegiate sports in Michigan are popular in addition to professional sports. The state\'s two largest athletic programs are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines" title="Michigan Wolverines">\n        Michigan Wolverines\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans" title="Michigan State Spartans">\n        Michigan State Spartans\n       </a>\n       , which play in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">\n        NCAA\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">\n        Big Ten Conference\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Stadium" title="Michigan Stadium">\n        Michigan Stadium\n       </a>\n       in Ann Arbor, home to the Michigan Wolverines football team, is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_stadiums" title="List of largest stadiums">\n        largest stadium in the Western Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       and the second-largest stadium worldwide behind\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rungrado_May_Day_Stadium" title="Rungrado May Day Stadium">\n        Rungrado May Day Stadium\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">\n        Pyongyang\n       </a>\n       , North Korea.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan_High_School_Athletic_Association" title="Michigan High School Athletic Association">\n        Michigan High School Athletic Association\n       </a>\n       features around 300,000 participants.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="State_symbols_and_nicknames">\n        State symbols and nicknames\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg/220px-Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg/330px-Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg/440px-Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dwarf_Lake_Iris.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dwarf_lake_iris" title="Dwarf lake iris">\n          Dwarf lake iris\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Michigan is, by tradition, known as "The Wolverine State," and the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">\n        University of Michigan\n       </a>\n       takes the wolverine as its mascot. The association is well and long established: for example, many Detroiters volunteered to fight during the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        American Civil War\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Armstrong_Custer" title="George Armstrong Custer">\n        George Armstrong Custer\n       </a>\n       , who led the Michigan Brigade, called them the "Wolverines". The origins of this association are obscure; it may derive from a busy trade in wolverine furs in\n       <a href="/wiki/Sault_Ste._Marie,_Michigan" title="Sault Ste. Marie, Michigan">\n        Sault Ste. Marie\n       </a>\n       in the 18th century or may recall a disparagement intended to compare early settlers in Michigan with the vicious mammal. Wolverines are, however, extremely rare in Michigan. A sighting in February 2004 near\n       <a href="/wiki/Ubly,_Michigan" title="Ubly, Michigan">\n        Ubly\n       </a>\n       was the first confirmed sighting in Michigan in 200 years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_154-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-msnbc-154">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The animal was found dead in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 27em; -webkit-column-width: 27em; column-width: 27em;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_nickname" title="State nickname">\n          State nicknames\n         </a>\n         :\n         <i>\n          Wolverine State\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <i>\n          Great Lake State\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <i>\n          Mitten State\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <i>\n          Water-Winter Wonderland\n         </i>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_mottos" title="List of U.S. state mottos">\n          State motto\n         </a>\n         :\n         <i>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Si_quaeris_peninsulam_amoenam_circumspice" title="Si quaeris peninsulam amoenam circumspice">\n           Si quaeris peninsulam amoenam circumspice\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         (Latin: "If you seek a pleasant peninsula, look about you") adopted in 1835 on the coat-of-arms, but never as an official motto. This is a paraphrase of the epitaph of British architect Sir\n         <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">\n          Christopher Wren\n         </a>\n         about his masterpiece,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St. Paul\'s Cathedral">\n          St. Paul\'s Cathedral\n         </a>\n         .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n          <a href="#cite_note-156">\n           [153]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n          <a href="#cite_note-157">\n           [154]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_song" title="State song">\n          State song\n         </a>\n         : "\n         <a href="/wiki/My_Michigan" title="My Michigan">\n          My Michigan\n         </a>\n         " (official since 1937, but disputed amongst residents),\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n          <a href="#cite_note-158">\n           [155]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         "\n         <a href="/wiki/Michigan,_My_Michigan" title="Michigan, My Michigan">\n          Michigan, My Michigan\n         </a>\n         " (Unofficial state song, since the civil war)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_birds" title="List of U.S. state birds">\n          State bird\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/American_robin" title="American robin">\n          American robin\n         </a>\n         (since 1931)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_mammals" title="List of U.S. state mammals">\n          State animal\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Wolverine" title="Wolverine">\n          wolverine\n         </a>\n         (traditional)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         State game animal:\n         <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_deer" title="White-tailed deer">\n          white-tailed deer\n         </a>\n         (since 1997)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_fish" title="List of U.S. state fish">\n          State fish\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Brook_trout" title="Brook trout">\n          brook trout\n         </a>\n         (since 1965)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_reptiles" title="List of U.S. state reptiles">\n          State reptile\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Painted_turtle" title="Painted turtle">\n          painted turtle\n         </a>\n         (since 1995)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_fossil" title="State fossil">\n          State fossil\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Mastodon" title="Mastodon">\n          mastodon\n         </a>\n         (since 2000)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_flowers" title="List of U.S. state flowers">\n          State flower\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">\n          apple blossom\n         </a>\n         (adopted in 1897, official in 1997)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         State wildflower:\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dwarf_lake_iris" title="Dwarf lake iris">\n          dwarf lake iris\n         </a>\n         (since 1998) a federally listed threatened species\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_trees" title="List of U.S. state trees">\n          State tree\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_white_pine" title="Eastern white pine">\n          white pine\n         </a>\n         (since 1955)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">\n          State stone\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Petoskey_stone" title="Petoskey stone">\n          Petoskey stone\n         </a>\n         (since 1965). It is composed of fossilized\n         <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">\n          coral\n         </a>\n         (\n         <i>\n          Hexagonaria pericarnata\n         </i>\n         ) from long ago when the middle of the continent was covered with a shallow sea.\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">\n          State gem\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Chlorastrolite" title="Chlorastrolite">\n          Isle Royale greenstone\n         </a>\n         (since 1973). Also called\n         <i>\n          chlorastrolite\n         </i>\n         (literally "green star stone"), the mineral is found on\n         <a href="/wiki/Isle_Royale" title="Isle Royale">\n          Isle Royale\n         </a>\n         and the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keweenaw_peninsula" title="Keweenaw peninsula">\n          Keweenaw peninsula\n         </a>\n         .\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/50_State_Quarters" title="50 State Quarters">\n          State quarter\n         </a>\n         : U.S. coin issued in 2004 with the Michigan motto "Great Lakes State".\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_soils" title="List of U.S. state soils">\n          State soil\n         </a>\n         :\n         <a href="/wiki/Kalkaska_sand" title="Kalkaska sand">\n          Kalkaska sand\n         </a>\n         (since 1990), ranges in color from black to yellowish brown, covers nearly 1,000,000-acre (4,000\xc2\xa0km\n         <sup>\n          2\n         </sup>\n         ) in 29 counties.\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" lower-alpha;">\n       <div class="mw-references-wrap">\n        <ol class="references">\n         <li id="cite_note-autogenerated2-7">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           ^\n           <a href="#cite_ref-autogenerated2_7-0">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               a\n              </b>\n             </i>\n            </sup>\n           </a>\n           <a href="#cite_ref-autogenerated2_7-1">\n            <sup>\n             <i>\n              <b>\n               b\n              </b>\n             </i>\n            </sup>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           Elevation adjusted to\n           <a href="/wiki/North_American_Vertical_Datum_of_1988" title="North American Vertical Datum of 1988">\n            North American Vertical Datum of 1988\n           </a>\n           .\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-9">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-9">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           <i>\n            i.e.\n           </i>\n           , including water that is part of state territory.\n           <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n            Georgia\n           </a>\n           is the largest state by land area east of the Mississippi and Michigan the second-largest.\n          </span>\n         </li>\n         <li id="cite_note-19">\n          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n           <b>\n            <a href="#cite_ref-19">\n             ^\n            </a>\n           </b>\n          </span>\n          <span class="reference-text">\n           The Province included the modern states of Wisconsin, eastern Minnesota, Illinois, Indiana, Ohio, Kentucky, Tennessee, Mississippi, Alabama, two-thirds of Georgia, and small parts of West Virginia, Pennsylvania, New York, Vermont, and Maine\n          </span>\n         </li>\n        </ol>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n
